O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine assembled from its employment, and I have finished it by its expositions and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it occurred to me that I would complete this treatise with this surgeon, which is part of the work of the hands, namely surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is difficult in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have followed
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the idleness, and the understanding is closed and the science is disordered.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I shall give life to this treatise in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and of abbreviation; and I shall join together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of the other instruments of this work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it befits him who meddleth in this work to be well acquainted with the science of anatomy, as Galen saith, so that he can judge of the members, and the forms and the joints and the separations of things, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and limbs and the number of bones, and the movement of the veins and the rest.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates taught us that the non-moving limb is useless, and the moving limb is useful; and in the art of healing the hand is like the other.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We are told in the beginning of this book that anyone who is ignorant of the things that lie before him, if he stirs up trouble and harms others, will learn many things of this science that he will abandon from lack of sense and understanding.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who, having copped a scrophule or the head of a woman, has coped the arteries of the neck; so that so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another time a stone of a bladder was extracted from a man, and the stone was great; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in his belly for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I have already been called to treat, and I saw the condition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and I knew that if it were pulled out, he would surely die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another time a man of our land took charge of a fracture of the limb and with splints made an incision; and the physicians were ignorant and stretched the fracture above the wound as if by strong binding, and left the wound without any bleeding, and left it thus until the limb was completely healed and the bone and flesh were lost forever
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I heard him call out and hurried to him; and when I arrived I found the limb dislocated without pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in every way it was already corrupted or limb was unsound; and I could not cure it; and the dislocation continued to grow until the limb was completely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another malady which engulfs the abdomen and encloses the veins, and then inflates because of the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is caused by melancholy humor, does not suffice to touch it with iron except in cases where it can remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, therefore, very heed the fact that the work of the hands has become divided into twelve parts: that is to say, huevre or there is peril in various situations; and I shall show in each part of this book where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you must keep your arms close to your body, so that the fools will not speak evil of you, take your weapons in your hands and treat your patients calmly and firmly, and use the best way so that by God's grace you may come out whole; and leave the dangerous diseases of grief behind; and reject that which makes you doubt, and be glad when you can escape from this world to the other, filled with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The fools speak harshly of you: “Do not take me for a cure for any ailment, for you will be remembered as a fool.”
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and medical leeching, and this chapter orders from the head downwards; and the forms of instruments, and the materials for cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work.</start_of_turn
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with amputation and incision, and wounds and abscesses, and the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; and this chapter orders and the forms of instruments.</start_of_turn>
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and fractures, as well as other similar matters; and it orders from the chief physician to have the limbs from the armpits downwards, and to form the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we have remembered from our work, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the aid and the danger of great complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the danger, is the most long speech and subtle science and the greatest secret response; and about these things they speak more often than others, and they agree among themselves; and I find that their words are often too long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or matter, for as much as .ij. complexions: that is to say complexion is hot with matter, and complexion is dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, assembled matter, some say that cautery is of great aid; others say that cautery is of no avail in disease except when it comes from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and must not be used to cure heat diseases by heat, nor by drought; and thus those who say the opposite that cautery does great aid in heat and dry diseases that arise from the humours of the body.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.</start_of_turn
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all the way, there stands between me and fire no one but he who has experienced it, and who knows by long observation the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of people’s complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the issues and means to prevent them; for other complexions we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them yield and agree to the cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, children, that fire cautery is better than any secret medicine or burning salve.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no harm to any member other than the one being treated.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines derived from one member to another cause ailments in the member by restoring health; and by chance the patient experiences pain. The fire of fever due to its height and the goodness of its substance does not make me do this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And thus I have learned through experience and the length of my service and study in this art, that it is true about things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to withhold the secret which is returned or the fire, and the quality of work, as it explains the healing of diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know then, son, when it comes to making cauteries, they must be done at a suitable tension and with caution.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, because the harmful effects which arise from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and even though the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait for a greater tension, more serious harm does not arise from the member.</start_of_turn>
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, dear son, that because fools make light of this; for the disease which is cured by cautery never returns; and he says so. But it is not so simple, for cautery is but a medicine which changes the complexion, and dries up humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its promptness, and for the excellence of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And indeed it is known that the disease does not arise at all according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and there are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of flesh and other things, if indeed cautery is administered in vain or if there is much superfluity and moisture, for in such a case the pain does not return; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand indeed that cautery is called the last of medicine, and indeed; but they do not believe that cautery is better than medicine, but their understanding is false, and indeed cautery is the last of medicine because when we administer other remedies in no illness and they do not help, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, although cautery is behind medicine, it does not agree with the intentions of the foolish masses.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery is duller than iron, and they do not say that fire is useful for aught other reason than the quality of the gold and the fineness of its substance; and they say that the bloodletting of cautery does not make much difference, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and I have found that it is seen in many people; and gold cautery is worth no more than iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how it is blackened by the color of gold, and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much; if there is too much fire; and thus there is enough impediment.</start_of_turn
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have observed in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from the head down to the feet, because for this reason the way is easier to find.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two things that cause it: a disease called "soda," and many humors that descend from the head downwards, causing swelling in the eyes, ears, and throat, and for many dreams and pain in the head and neck, and even for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.</start_of_turn>
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	When the patient is purged by means of a medicinal solution modifying the head, iij or iiij, as the physician deems necessary and as the patient's condition permits, then make the patient spit out the head again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then sit the patient comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his armpits; after that place the root of your thumb on the root of his nipple between his two armpits; and there will come out his two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the root then pull out the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and do descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then hold your hand loosely, and restore the limb if you see the bone even a little; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take out one’s thumb, and place cotton wool around and under, and then take out the limb, and leave it for two days; after that put on a warm compress and cover with a bandage, and leave it as long as the swelling has gone down. Then cure the wound which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the elders, that the more time that passes over a wound, the more it purges; and for this reason help is needed.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must leave the cautery on for so long that any part of the bone is scorched, and then we must renew what is scorched from the bone, and it must be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say others that we must leave the cautery on for so long, and press so hard that we break off as much bone as a woman puts in her fuse for the sake of these humors that come out too much; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; and then we must cure and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be of much use in all cases, for in some men or when there is danger; and I believe that I must leave it; for the pain of the patient is often excessive from the continuing solutions of nature, as we can see in other members; and even when the pain of the patient is slight by nature, the first sign of the cautery is more beneficial and more soothing for me, and for this reason I will use it in these cases.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times, pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain persists in the head for a long time, the physician should use leech therapy, pills called "cochie," and purgatives for the head, oil and poultices; and if the fire cautery is done as we have said, it is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's condition is very severe, and do not burn too deeply; for otherwise the cautery will be of no benefit.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have cauterized up to the bone of the head as we have said, do cautery of the vein which is called "vasselz"; and keep your hand still so that you do not move until you reach the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is better to cauterize the corners than the middle of the head, for the latter is how it is formed:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in the chief [shoulder], and the disease extends to the root, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicinal means, and other cures have been made as mentioned in the division of diseases, and all this has not helped: then make cautery in two ways, namely by means of medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicinal cautery is to take an alexanders root, and extract the bark and scrape it; if there are two heads of the shoulder, then make the temple where the pain persists as much as you can until the alexanders root is withdrawn from the skin; and when it is withdrawn, if you bind and constrain it well and leave it for fifteen hours; then remove it and treat the root with vinegar and leave the wound for two or three days; then put on a compress soaked in oil until it covers the whole part.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans. Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in order; and hold his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, do not move his head; then put cotton wool soaked in egg or in vinegar on the oil; then burn the cautery that is partly: and let it rest on the head as if it were a feather of wool, gather up what is around it so that it is the cautery; if you see, if there is a point of the head that has bled from the other, and if you see that there is as much as a tendril; but all this is worth as much as your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells out, and in going through the swelling, and the dryness; and if it closes, if the wound, and go out violently the hair; afterwards put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part where there is no feeling behind the oil, that your hand does not move foolishly; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you approach the beginning of the cautery right up to the bone, that would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not happen, if you must repeat the cautery once more, and if you must do it a third time, leave it for three days; after that, put on a wet compress over the burn, and let the drying ointment heal as long as it is healthy; if forty days pass and it is still unhealthy, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is discovered; and then proceed as is customary in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients have mentioned
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	With fistula, and open the vessel; after that, put in the gap one small camphor cube, which is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it in the amount of a third of a palm; and keep your hand or bandage firmly, and do not move the patient in any way, except that the melted wax runs down to its oil; and it is recommended to put above the oil to the patient a wet cotton pad in the bin of urine or in awe: the wax is so apt to flow like a fistula, and the rest for a marvel of health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, then it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if that does not happen, if you must give an incision to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its proper place as you see fit in your own work.
des crevaices en levres	from cracks in the liver
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there arise cracks in the limbs which are called "hair", and even in the limbs of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks in the way we have said in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you must perform a small burn cautery according to this fashion:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And hold the burn firmly in those cracks until it is healed; after curing the limb until it is whole again.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the armpit of the shoulder
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the root of the tooth comes loose from the gum, or from the eye, or from the palate, or from the root of the teeth, after that it causes decay and pain and becomes swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the blood stops flowing from the wound; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is healed once, it is good; and if it is not healed, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the root of the tooth comes loose from the gum, or from the eye, or from the palate, or from the root of the teeth, after that it causes decay and pain and becomes swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the blood stops flowing from the wound; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is healed once, it is good; and if it is not healed, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in this chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have cured it by medicine and this does not help, then put the patient’s head in your hand; after that remove the cautery which formed previously in this part as much as you can without causing pain; put some ointment into the cautery while it is still hot, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that release your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part of the manner in which it was moving, if it is confirmed, and the joint becomes soft and restricted, and moisture becomes dry and corrupted.
de la dolor des dens	And in part of the manner in which it was moving, if it is confirmed, and the joint becomes soft and restricted, and moisture becomes dry and corrupted.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and the remedies of medicine do not suffice, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the burr and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If the burr is like that which is taken from the navel of a calf, and the end is put in a spoon of iron or lead; after that take cotton and wrap over the point of a needle, and the soft matter in the burr is bulged out, and put on the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cooled; and do this often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see if soft matter slips out and cotton in the burr is rough, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the flesh comes to the height of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery, when it is made of fire as is like taking tongs of iron or brass, and be large so that the fire does not reach the patient’s mouth; then burn the cautery until it forms, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, for the pain will be great at first or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you must make the patient swallow well with good burp in the heat of the cautery, and then hold it firm; and this is the form of the cautery
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Burn as much as you please, and according to what you desire; and that is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	And the size upon the perforated bone and the moisture, if it is lighter, because they are of little blood. And if there are any of these perforations or heads or if there is no moisture, and of these are those which I cauterize or heads of an old woman; and find the perforation as with a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it. And if no bleeding has occurred from it, one must make as good a wound as if it were a stone. In other perforations coming or heads, forasmuch as these which come from the heads of the children and have roots of the ears, it opens if it is at all possible every day at the most dependent time, for fear of causing a swelling; and it heals as it should.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is composed of phlegm and cold moisture, and is not subject to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the cautery needle quickly; for it will take its form immediately, and cause two abscesses from the fumes to rise to the cautery on the other side; and place the cautery hot on the abscess once, or if it mixes, until it reaches the head of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, evacuate the cautery as much as the quantity of the abscess demands, and leave it for three days; and apply moist cotton on the wound until the swelling has subsided.
Li forme de la cainne:	The formation of the cancrum.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels due to a cold complexion, it is necessary to evacuate the patient first with resolving medicines; then apply the cautery to the root of the throat, and keep it until it reaches the throat, without going further downwards; for there is danger in doing so
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, I shall perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone and the head of the scapula; and let the cautery which is called the "clavile" be as before; and cure the limb as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores and the same comes from a cold complexion, then it is expedient that the patient be first relieved by soluble medicines. Then perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go further down to the throat, and do not linger there more than necessary. Then perform another cautery at the joint of the neck to the chest, and the one which is called the "clavicle" is like this; and cure the wound as we have said above until it is healed
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every ailment of the pores is of cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and is an ancient disease, if you do him an ipecacatory on the forcele in his veins; and another ipecacatory between two mamils; or let the ipecacatory which is called "claw" according to the shape which is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a cautery by pricking with all the cautery which is called "points" of which the form is as before in the ear disease; and let the points be until XXX, or as much as is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After that, cure the limb as we have said before, and let the cautery be done three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of this, the cautery is lighter, because you do two at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, hold the patient on their back and on their side; then take the thumb that is inside the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, if it is shifted, insert the cautery as it is, without causing any damage: that is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the thumb until it reaches the ribs, and the escape of the cautery would be three cauteries; and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery which has two needles, because the figures of cauterization are these two cauteries; and these nerves are according to the delicacy of a try and this is the form of the cautery which has two needles:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is the suture placed upon this vein for there are six cauteries there.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then put on the cautery and burn the brozed hair with care; after that, rest the patient and do not move the limb until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated below, whatever the cause, then make a cautery on the edge of the "clavile" cautery, or do several pricks.</start_of_turn
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is bony, and the pain is relieved.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and moist emissions come from the stomach, and they irritate its surface, they cause many discharges, and are customary treatments that do not help; therefore, it is necessary that the patient rest on his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Afterwards, make three cauteries: one on the navel and two on the ribs, as much as a clove of garlic. At every cautery, keep the needle clasped, and make two cauteries on the two costal bones so that the figures of the cauteries form an angle of three, and there should be some space between them so that they do not touch each other when they swell; and let the cauteries be so strong that they cause the two parts of the liver to swell, and let the figure of the cauteries resemble this form in shape from front to back
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if thou seest cauterized with a great cautery in the stomach as aforesaid; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and sign upon the stomach in a point according to the quantity which thou seest of hair; then cauterize the whole of the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the cure which we have seen before, as long as he is well.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain of fruit and moisture and great swelling, as long as it is forced from its natural complexion by the superabundances; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and he does not benefit from it, if he is not restored to his habitus; and signs of hair three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, to drive away the spleen, the liver or the testicles of the man; and let there be space between each cautery the thickness of a bean; and let the cautery be long as the nail of the thumb, and do not press too hard with your hand over the whole cautery; and let only half of the burn be blackened, and let the patient lie down on his side; and if he cannot, if so, let him stretch out his legs, and hold his arms; and that is the form.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you are tempted, if these cauteries are too delicate, if you are unskilled and ignorant in this art, beware lest you mar your entire body, for you will burn away all your flesh; and it will not cease until it boils, for the flesh is too subtle in that place, and the veins are liable to burst.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is swelling on the liver, and you know whether it is in the liver itself or in the gall: if it is in the liver, the patient feels little pain; but if it is in the gall, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	When this treatment is completed, if you believe the patient is cured of his head wound; then sign the limb or the swelling is gone, and then burn the cautery which is similar in shape to a thorn, for this is the proper form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And I cauterize thus far as the hairs are thick and strong, and come to an end just as the hair has reached its full growth; and when the hair has been plucked at its root, I hold the eyes steady until it has grown. After that, I cure in the usual way until the wound is healed; and I command thee that you use this cautery only for such things as a man who has studied long and diligently in the art of medicine, and by whom these diseases have never been corrected.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, he must be wary of working too carelessly, and I think that in this matter it would be better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of a pleuraisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old folk said that we must make at pleasure cauteries of elder root, and in part thus: take an elder root long, the greatest that you can find, and be dry, and be as thick and long as your thumbs; and moisten in oil, and stamp on the fire, and cauterize. i. cauterize between the nipple and the belly, and ii. a few cauteries one inch in descending in the part which is below the beard; and iii. cauterize between the fifth rib and the twelfth, declining behind one inch. i. cauterize the spleen, and i. another upon the stomach, and i. between two ribs, and i. two ribs as many costae as go before the cautery that is between two ribs; and do not press me your hand, but open thus as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no former has ever used a fire cautery like this, which resembles a razor, and which is put between the ribs, until it comes to this abscess; and sudden pain follows, as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies immediately, or an abscess comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	The mouse is small and delicate,
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the mouse's disease as we have said, and it does not profit, then two cautery methods remain good.

de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
