Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And thus Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with cloves of chive, if it helps with moisture; and it must be done cautiously in parts
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in much oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the big toe and the one that is called the fossilized pit.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking cloves of chive dry, and burning them until they are charcoal, and then putting them on the lint, and letting them stay until they are stained; then do it again, and do not stop doing it until you think that it is enough until the swelling has gone down and the pain has ceased; and this method of cautery is called "cautery of chive".
de la dolor dou dos	From the pain of the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar symptoms of cold matter spread, neither of these signs is worth cautery, except for what comes from the infusion of cold matter.</start_of_turn>
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be devoid of stinking pills or other symptoms, that one be made on his back, lying down or where the pain persists, for three lines marked with a needle, and in between one line. Five cauteries or more according as the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the point which is called “needle”; and if you see, make two or three cauteries at the middle point of the needle according to this form:</start_of_turn
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that it hurts the skin when it is struck, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you witness its cure, if you cauterize with the fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns any part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	If you see that the burn penetrates too deep into the spine, cauterize around the spine two or three lines below the point where the burn penetrates. Keep the points close together.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treatment, keep the limb sound as we have said, and beware that you do not bring too much cautery near the nerves.</start_of_turn
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain originates from a wound, the sufferer cries out "podagre" thus; when the cause is cold and the disease does not yield to medicines, it may be cured by cautery in part: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the limb, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the bone, if you cauterize with all the cautery that you claim “point”.</start_of_turn
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the shoulders and to other joints, and this happens many times, if you cauterize on each shoulder three cauteries or four of each part, with all the olive oil; and if you must do more, do more, but do not hold your hand too long that the skin should burn.</start_of_turn
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as far as the hands, if you prick twice in the flesh; and if there is no more pain, prick on the wrist and on the little finger of the hand; and if the pains go down to the buttocks or to the shoulder blades, cauterize some part of it, and give the patient good treatment and prescribe medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good treatment and purge phlegm, it will be well with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	then they are dry and do not require aid.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones slip downwards as in a wound, this is new; if you see that it is cured, do not move it immediately; and do not use things that leave your belly open, so that the intestines descend from your belly; afterwards make it sit on its belly between your hands, and command that it hold its shoulder tight until the bones are repaired, and keep it fixed at your sides, and mark an indentation of the nail on the scapula at the level of the collarbone, and as much as a half circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery as it is.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is limp and lets sense smell.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then keep the buttocks still in their place; and he should hold your hand so that they do not go back; and give the patient good treatment of the wound, and put a cushion for him under the hips and under the hands; and another under his wrist; then put the cautery on the sign at the top of the hand, and hold it straight and hold it for as long as you can until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware attentively that the butt does not swell when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that in this way the patient does not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And nails that until they reach the bone at the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is commanded that the cautery of the nails should be subtle in measure of the small, and of the great people also in measure; after three days cure the limb of the cautery of burr until the scab is bony; after cure other ointments until it is healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well healed; and it is commanded that his movements be calmed in length, so that the swelling does not go out when he is about to walk into the chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, let him have a good meal ready, and keep him for forty days; and give him rest, that he work little and take care of himself from too great a drinking of wine and eating, and from too great a lifting of burdens; and when he has done this teaching if he is completely healed.</start_of_turn>
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the cure of the tail in its chapter afterwards.
de la routure dou ventre	of the evacuation of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come out in other parts and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow any more, then you shall make the burn of the burn again according to their quantity, and be three parts of the fourth; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one has said before that it should be burned with the burn at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the limb of the shoulder and make a line perpendicular to the breadth below the wound, and another at a distance, and hold your hand firmly against the entire burn with the clamp of the burn
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first burns are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in no limb.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, or in the shoulder or in the wound, and this pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment does not suffice, then it is necessary to burn it with the burn which is called "points", and the burn must be made according to the length of the limb and the size and weakness and virtue and location of the swelling and the pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery on that one, for it is customary that it must move towards the adjacent part, so that you may make the cauteries as long as the patient remains sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, or from sitting or injury, and the pain persists, and medical treatment is of no avail, then it is expedient that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with other cauteries according to the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is healed after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure once more, for it is customary to burn the surrounding area until the patient is healed.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease never helps itself with a cautery, and the same ailment that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cautery being made? Take notice if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not stay or depart, and you doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the whole sickness, then make five cauteries on the head: one at the new root, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the beard; and two on the two corners, and one behind on the heel; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the pus comes out forcefully so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is sparse throughout; and it is clearly visible, if you deem that you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, namely: one on the crown of the head, two on the shoulder blades, three on the spine of the neck, four on the buttocks, five on the groin, six on the elbows, seven on the wrists, eight on the fingers, and nine on the toes; and beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bones of the heel or the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the boils that the more he does of the cautery, the more he does of aid, and benefits him; and the boils that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery, as if he felt it, because the carbuncle is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery should be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you observe in the handling of things.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, leave the wound covered with flour for some time with honey and other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and dressings, and is not well, then you must make cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery penetrate as deep as the nerve; then treat with ointments until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never is fire cautery done with hand or foot or back, at the issue of nerves that move the limb, and so if it be osseus it swells; and in every case nothing should intervene except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of nerves moving the limb.
de albaras	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is ordered to perform cautery on the limb according to the extent and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery penetrate deep into the flesh as much as possible. Then treat the wound until it is healed. And under no circumstances shall cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the risk of damaging the nerve that moves the limb, or if the swelling is bony. And in all cases, do not interfere with the swelling unless you are familiar with the limb and the course of its moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then it is ordered to cauterize with a needle a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the marrow is white and solid; and then treat with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it at rest until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you cauterize with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that it is done in the middle of the boil; and in my opinion it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already known of several cases where it has happened; and the safer thing is to cauterize around it, with the cautery which is called the "circle," as we have said previously
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an ailment that is called "adubelati", and it is late to recover or due to the excessive speed with which it progresses or because the patient has lost too much blood, or for some other tension; and you see that it is urgent to recover: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; and leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to recover.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her perish with all the cautery, if she is burning too much, make the cautery less: for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment that is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have perceived the pain, and be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in parts as the disease progresses
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then leave it until it is perfectly healed
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another symptom of disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing other than a weakening of the limbs, because it makes them soft like dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in which you can perform the whole cautery together with fire, then you must shave the hair closely and abundantly, according to what is convenient for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains except for the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs a broth of oil until the blisters caused by the fire are ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of these wounds with oil, there remains char.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hair does not grow back, it is good; but if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on what remains unscarred.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This torment never finds its cure in water medicine except for fire cautery; but all the same, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of water medicine in the section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when a piece has fallen out of place, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing that causes the limb to swell up
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	If thou art scorched with fire, I shall teach thee how to cauterize as with a pen of goosefoot. Make it of fine iron of the size that can pierce through all parts, and let there be small margins; then put all about the wound, and hold thy hand quite over the wound until it comes to the front of the wound; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to fester. Then make an embolus of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leave the embolus upon the wound all night, and bind it firmly and it shall be loosened from its root.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of swelling by raising it as high as possible until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if there are converted by boils which often happen in hands and feet, if you must bring about a cure, apply a hot cautery; and in part: take a flaxseed or iron needle or a goosefoot pen, and place over the wound and the fat, that is to say, around the nails; and put the bandage over so that it covers all around, then put on a little of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the bandage comes to the root of the wound, and may find the hot water way through to the root; and offer the patient a little of the hot water an hour; then leave it alone, and it will burst out all at its roots.

li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide. des pustules puans	When anyone trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever, or from any other cause, if you shall make for him three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery on the flank and one on the stomach at the olive cautery, he will recover from the cold sickness.

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	For if it is not secured, if you do not hold it tight without doubt in all things. And they call it the ancient 'cure contuse', and that you make at the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has or front, then make three incisions or front evenly according to the length of the front; and let one of the incisions be as two teeth do all together downwards to the navel, and the others two as two ribs by the papers, and keep the incision of the arteries that are as two ribs by the papers; and align your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let there be about three wounds in quantity at the crossing of the joints; and have learned a piece of sponge and cloth of cloth to soak up the blood, then bind the bandage tightly in two parts of the way that is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple down to the second incision; and scrape out all the marrow which is between the two incisions up to the bone, then make the other half of the wound down to the other second, and then pull out this clot.</start_of_turn>
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and which is very well cut on one side and slightly blunt on the other, is not sufficiently cutting, it is like this:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the incision is continuous until it reaches the marrow at the head, and then finish by cutting in the middle fissure until the other end; then drain the blood equally, and express the marrow out of the bone with the blood taken; then put in the wound a little piece of felt, and cover with moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and herbs, and keep that there are no further haemorrhages; and after three days take out the stitches, and give strong medicines of aquatint, and treat the wound with basilic ointment with rosemary oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	since the evacuation of blood
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is done, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilate, and the papers burn; and the hair cries out, and where it has been pricked, it causes acute pain, and the patient coughs; then there are discharges from these accidents except for those of matters and catarrh that come from many veins, and it brings relief that it is so.

When it is fixed, make sure you rub the bone until it begins to heal, and then treat it with drying agents, which make it harden.

In part: take three parts of flour of wheat and three parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it on these wounds to cause the pain to disappear throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	because of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever is causing the swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or a stone or some other object like iron; or semen, like in the case of lice, beans, peas; or something that flows downwards like blood and pus and other things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When the head of the ear cartilage or some other object that does not fit into the ear, does not enter the ear, place the ear on the sole.

If you see the cartilage [of the ear], if no black pustule or sesame oil comes out, then order its extraction; and make him cough out phlegm, and stop his nose when he coughs, and put cotton wool around the ear and hold it up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times blood comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, order its extraction with fine needles, as this is its form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, remove it with fine tweezers. And if it does not come out by this method, make an incision at the root of the ear, or cut away a part of the ear, and stop up the hole with wax if necessary; then the pain will go away, for often it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the ear and press on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in haste to make an incision at the earlobe as at the base of the thumb, and spasm, and the method of the incision is that you make first the chief sufferer endure the pain of the cephalic region, and draw out blood according to the measure of its virtue; then seat the sufferer between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fatty tissue or bone depending; and make the incision as wide as a crescent moon, as long as you live to the bone, and the bone according to your ability, and extract the pus promptly from your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is grains that are swollen and it swells, if you administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, if you advise .i. sponge held tightly according to this form:

de l’estoupement des oreilles	because of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same happens among adults by the bursting of a wound or by a foreign body entering the ear. Such bursts never happen without leaving some mark in the ear, if we do not see them; and never happens without some loss of hearing.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which leaves a mark in the ear, if we do not see it, is a sign of serious illness in various conditions, and in this one it is clear that you put the diseased ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the swelling, if the swelling has filled the whole cavity, like this is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be cautious both front and back all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the swelling is of a foreign body in the ear, if you see small incisions, and if you touch it lightly, as long as the foreign body is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incisions are too deep in the ear, take a slight scraper and burn the edge with a small fire, then put in or remove the dressing of the ear.</start_of_turn

If you feel the swelling which the patient has at the ear, pierce slightly, and keep your hand away from the ear nerves; then insert a plug according to the size of the perforation, and moisten with Egyptian unguent.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la char des papieres	De la char des papieres.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	From the heap of papers

And if it is not well cured, if the fire cautery is applied too late after the incision is made, it is of no use; and often the roots are burned and do not recover again.
de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come together on paper scraps things which seem to writhe in their form and their hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granulation", and is an assembly of large moisture in the substance of the wound; the work is like this: take hold of the granulation if it moves from one side to the other, and it is a light matter to know; then make the opening wide, then gently scratch the surrounding area, then take tweezers and grasp.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not perceive its cover to be lost, if it does not grieve the patient; and if the wound is large, if the assembly has a bolster, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for it will restore itself immediately and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granuloma descends downwards from the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the body, and pull out the granuloma with tweezers, and press from one side and the other; and if the body is loosened by the incision, this does not grieve; and when the granuloma is grasped, if it leaves oily water, cure the body of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is enclosed in paper tissues, and this happens more in those who have no nails, grieve moist at their eyes, and come to the bath in the morning, and do not dare to look at the sunlight for that their tears run from their eyes; and because they lie down with their faces down, and sleep on their backs, and their papers stick to their eyelashes moistened by the oil that appears on them.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand to your chest and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient places their head in its proper place; then take one drape of linen and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of exudate from the lower part of the body, and put it on top; and press on the body from one side and the other, so that the exudate is gathered into the circle; then make a small incision at the edge of the moisture trenching a wound not larger than the wound made to the vein; and make the skin taut as much as you see to the exudate; and in various situations there comes exudate from the wound, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the fatty substance from all around your thumbs between your shoulders, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as necessary; and keep that you do not insert anything into the wound, that you do not go too far up to the oil, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, if you cut a little around the wound slightly until it opens; then take out the foreign body as we have said, then moisten the bandage and water, and put on the limb, and strain it carefully.

Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the vein being cut above, if the treatment of closing wounds is applied as soon as it is sane.
des poilz des papieres	of hair papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hair growing other than its natural way, and are overgrown, if they prick the eyes, they cause tears and bring on various diseases like common tears and softening of papers and gum, up to the point of destroying the eyes; the cure for this is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and suture or by ligature, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient’s head in your left hand, and move the paper from the oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a thorn at any point of the paper, either cut the edge of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs; and take out one thread from the underside of the paper, and stretch out the paper from the underside, from the great to the small; then take out the one thread, and put some small lint and bandage on the paper, and make a mark on the paper like the spur of a myrtle, and when you have made the mark it is understood that the paper that was destined to you is no longer there.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it comes to the vein being cut above, if the treatment of closing wounds is applied as soon as it is sane. If there is much bleeding, according to what is written above, then make a large incision two lines below the wound; and begin with great bleeding until little; and let the vein bleed out from its natural orifice, then apply the ointment to one of the two angles towards the front, then remove the clot; then sew up the two layers with a needle of fine thread, and dry the wound. If you see this done; if not, leave the stitches in place for three days or four; then cure the wound with dry and constrictive things, because the blood will naturally gather under the wound and reunite the edges, but the stitches are useless (as they say in ancient times), and that is harmful; and if there is another method: let the blood flow from the vein by making a mark on it that is as big as a berry, as we have said, and let three ounces of blood drain out according to the shape that is mentioned.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then hold back what is above with small forces equally according to the shape which is like this
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the teeth steady, and the matter is not even, take a needle or two and pass one thread through the large hole and the second through the small; gather the two threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the surrounding skin together as we have described; then assemble the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, apply cerate and similar soothing poultices. Never again shall you see hair of the beard converted: if you follow what we have said concerning the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for armpits is as follows: convert the hair and fat according to what has been said, and then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the hair and expand with space; and take three hairs or hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other securely above what rests on the oil of the hair. Strain the three hairs from the three parts forming; and leave it like that for a few days, and the skin which has been strained will become wrinkled and necrotic and will swell, until it comes loose by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, or if the wound has great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed and the wound dressing has been removed, the hair will no longer grow. This is the shape of two nails that you will make in this figure and in this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is in it a thread of silken stuff; then assemble the joints and do not leave one without the other, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then command in the chase another thread of silken stuff briefly, and do not leave the head of the thread; then put the patient's head in its place; and let there be daylight if the work is done carelessly, for it is a subtle and small work; then withdraw the needle to the very root of the hair, and make it pierce in the flesh until you have driven it as much as the natural position of the hair; then withdraw the hair until it is gone from the chase, and bring back into the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the blood vein flees to the very chase in the flesh with the natural position of the hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you drive the chase from its end to the very thread that you have commanded, until the chase blood comes out through the wound and you see it by the sight of the oil; then if you drive the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has regained its place and the swelling has gone down.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the fester comes to the boil, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there follows by consequence of wound, or of burn or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of working in it is that you close the wound, dry the flesh, put in stitches of linen, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything else except use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, if the disease comes back worse than before; but it is necessary to do soft things, like fennel; and mustard seed or alum and linseed oil be boiled, and oil of diaquilon melted in no oil, and it covers a bandage, and treat with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the cauldron which comes in the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is often called "axacrati", is natural and sudden.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cut and burn and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that if you take an awl, because it has two files, and the file on the heel, it makes the left eye weep so much that the file of the vein is in two pieces of the heel; then the heel is above all the awl, and the handle has one large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb returns according to what is commanded, that is good; if not, take an awl and put it in the incision, and twist the limb, and make two incisions or break the bone inside the limb; and if there are two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have made, or make one angle so that when they are put together, the limb is as well formed as a letter that has not "I grieve"; then fix that limb according to the quantity of its cost and weight, of what is useful to support the limb, then rejoin the two broken parts, and bind them with a thread of linen; then cure what we have said of the medicines that are softening, and of supports, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the malady comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a full incision around the hairs of paper; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the malady, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive very well all sorts of things how to make return to their natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what must be done of work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the malady comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a full incision around the hairs of paper; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the malady, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive very well all sorts of things how to make return to their natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what must be done of work and instruments in various dispositions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has to be done at home in a rather clumsy way as when the patient’s limb is soothed with oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, if you must therefore drink the tip of a needle from the wound and hold it high; and as soon as you see bruising, as long as you can keep within the limit of the sensitive area, which is not too deep and not too shallow, so that the patient does not suffer too much from the bruising or from the oil; and your incision, which you must make with care, so that the tissues are not too tight or too loose, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and when all the tissues are stitched up again, do not put in any more salt-water, but rather water that is soft and soapy; then put between the limb and the oil a bandage of linen, and cover the oil with thick wool; and after that use a bandage of wool and other soft things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Saiches that the nail is according to two methods: it is nervous and seems like tough wax, and another which is not very nervous, but seems like pale moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and boils it, it does not move; and both seem to begin towards the great tear, and twist about as much as they cover all the eye and the light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient puts his head in a straight line, then opens the eyes; and keep your hand on the cheek, and then I will grasp the nail with small double pliers, and extend it upwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and stitch it firmly to the nail, and pierce through all the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upwards, and wash away all the surrounding hair from the nail that encompasses the pulp and the skin to the hair, and leave the natural or oily discharge, if there is no discharge of tears usually from the incision; and in no case should the nail be extended only with the needle and thread, as we have said; then the wash away all the surrounding hair so that this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the thick cloth and break it, and that the needle does not pierce through; and after the incision, pour oil a spoonful of bruised oil into the wound, and sprinkle it with alum, and leave it until the other day; then cure what is left until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if the patient suffers, pour oil the patient’s body, and take the sponge lightly as required in this fashion:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail subtly, and if you see that it has diminished point and the edge is pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil alum, and sprinkle it with red alum and bruised oil, and squeeze out the oil until the other day; then repeat the other work as required in this manner.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you, if like an abscess you have opened, then milk, and first close the wound thoroughly while it is healthy, and afterwards resume the work as before, while it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If at night in the oil appears fat tissue with great swelling, if you suspend it at the ointment, and take a part and not all, that tears of tears do not arise; then distill in the red oil of colocynth which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the seed that grows on the plum.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you feed the treatment with weak oil from the natural way; and from an accident, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is relaxed from that work.
des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The wounds are red veins that are covered with oil, and they tolerate the gaze of the patient and expand the oil all day long.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The master is thus from the first that you look at the oil, in which the wound is, is strong, and there is no other disease fierce than the wound; therefore you must take part: instruct the patient to put his head in his health, then suspend those veins to the utmost extent according to his wisdom, and be the sutures subtle doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be doubled in degrees by degrees in a circle according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And suspend those veins silently by degrees in a circle according to this form: then bind as tightly as forces those veins silently, and evacuate the blood an hour later, as long as you see those veins leaving the oil; and keep that the oil does not touch the tips of the nails, and make this work at noon before the sun, and be calm and steadfast in your work if you do not wish to break anything except those veins; and when you have done this, if there is anything that remains doubtful, distill in the green and red oil to correct what is remaining doubtful.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all this in that hour, if you make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is appeased and is secured after the cautery, then begin again according to this method as long as you are well; and this is the way of forces:

de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not more fierce than a wound which is assembled in oil, resembling descending water, and it is not actually pain; and the method of its appearance is that if you make the patient sit on a chair which appears straight, and take hold of the head between your hands two parts, and move the limb until you see the wound coming down towards your eyes; then either bind it tightly, or do not remove the light and see the patient's condition as he is alone; and if it does not descend spontaneously, it is like acute pain, and if it descends from the wound it is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards on the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. If nothing remains to be done, if the incision has reached its utmost extent, if nothing remains to hold; and if without delay you do not sew it up or ligate it, or if you delay too long, or if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize it while it is still unstained, and remove all the purulent matter. Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises in the neck a disease which is called «telul», and it grows and becomes great again, so that it is seen; and for this reason it is necessary that you commence to apply the cautery or burning medicine at once, and extract the bone thoroughly, then bring forth the hair or scorched matter; and if you delay in covering it while it is great, if there is any hardness, of foul colour, or loss of sensation: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a dangerous abscess, for whenever it is touched even once, there results great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul colour, you will see that you can cover it completely, if you leave the patient and cover it without pain, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.

This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which we distill oils and medicines or the like.
