At home, in the hands of the patient, are placed the apices of the thumbs, resembling grains of wheat, minor and major; therefore it is to be known that you must turn the thumbs, make incisions upon each nail, and grasp them with tweezers and press them into the flesh; then apply the leech after the incision of the vitriole broth, until the wound is no longer bleeding; then remove the leech easily, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Concerning the pain of the jaws.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens that on the teeth of the jaw, which are called “albulus” by the ancients, there is pain; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or the blood out; then put out the vitriole broth or other restorative and drying powders; and if the tooth comes out again after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not come out again after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments to cover.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	The teeth are often gathered at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are rough and biting; and never are the teeth black and yellow and turned towards, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if it is thought that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be steady, and open the jaws or the gums, until nothing remains; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if we did that from the beginning, that would be good; if not, if you repeat it twice or three times, until you have done everything. And the teeth that have been mixed with various forms of instruments to redden them, as it is shown by the work, for those that remove the teeth have other forms than those that are used between the teeth; and these forms and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is appropriate when you cure the tooth of its pain that you also delay a little so that it does not hurt too much, because it must not be done carelessly; for it is a high-quality substance, so we have no excuse for making it suffer
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that they will endure.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient experiences pain, and take care that it is neither too great nor too little, and make them endure the pain of the bone; and although the pain does not depart from them because of this, as long as the malady persists, for we have already wanted to make them suffer in these matters; and when you are well certain that they will endure, if you escort the limb towards all its spasms, stretch it strongly to ward off the swelling of all parts; then hold your hand over the two thumbs and index fingers from the first joint and joint, until they are well displaced; and then tighten the bandages firmly. And be sure the patient’s limb is positioned between your thighs, and hold it firmly so that it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, draw the tooth straight out towards the front; and if it does not come out immediately, take none of these instruments and hold it loosely in the cheek; and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is grasped and twisted, if you can, fill it with cloth, either inside or outside; and if the force is applied too hard, that it breaks; and you must keep your mouth moist over the gum by scraping the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some, and return to the patient by the greatest pain of the first.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be aware that you must not act carelessly like the ignorant fools, who break the limb at every opportunity without reason, and bring no benefit to anyone; but they bring disaster every time because of the root of this great disease caused by the fracture of the limb itself, as we have often said; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the blood of wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is blood, as it often happens, apply a little vitriol; and if that does not suffice, cauterize.</start_of_turn
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they may remain silent at first, shall be long pointed and broad-handed, so that they do not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of fine iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the back, if you must take out the moist cotton swab, do so with a forceps or something similar.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is flexible, since the teeth are loose which are called "algefri", the head of the humerus appears like a beak of a thrush; and they must be made as with a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not suffice to hold all these tensions, if you must uncover the marrow throughout the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", namely a palatine, for this is its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large if it does not break me, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, if you support all the instruments, for in this way the shapes will come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has two rains, for this is its form
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears irregularly, its form is unsightly, even in women of gentle character, if it is known that it will not emerge fully from its socket and is not properly aligned, it should be extracted. If it is affected with the tooth, take hold of this instrument which has a small beak-like projection, and be careful not to break the bone.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And when the tooth persists in the gums and hands are clasped for a long time due to the duration of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you are using a file similar to this one which has the same shape.</start_of_turn>
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like the file which we use for nails; and while gently gripping the tooth and hands for a while, if it does not move as much as it aches, then at the end we can remove all the roughness, so that it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.</start_of_turn>
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth comes loose, by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it except when biting, and if you treat it with restrictive medicines, this is of no use; for if you order to restrain it with a golden thread, because the silver thread turns green and corrupts, but the bone does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are properly aligned, if you take hold of the thread and pass it double between the two front teeth, and then place the teeth between the front teeth, if there are one or more of them, until you see them clearly up to the next tooth; then repeat the covering until you reach the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, until it does not move; and let your thread be fixed to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the shoulder and put it in a clamp, assemble and reassemble between the teeth of the jaw, and hold it in place so that it does not bleed the tongue; and then leave it in place as tightly as it can stay in place, and if it slips or the head of the shoulder breaks, if the strain of another thread; if it remains and serves in its place, this is the form of wisdom and the figure of the arrangement of the two upper teeth and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing intervene except what is wise and soothing, and never make the form of a tooth like a bone spur, and put it back in the place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it so tight as we have said, for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes the tongue or nature itself causes the loosening of the teeth; or by an accidental wound; and the work is such that you must cause the patient to spit out the tongue, and place your hand on his jaw, and hold the tongue; then take the large nerve of the lip, as long as the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there is any duration or difficulty, and this is a sign of wound, if it has burst and you must bind the wound and take hold of the lip; and keep the wound from being too deep, for the artery which is loosened; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale and easy swelling, or a cold swelling, then spit out the tongue with a little tension; and hold the patient’s cheek closed at night, so that the tongue will not swell again.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if discharge of blood comes, if put out the glass vial broken; and if it does not go away, if cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it of other cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a reddish or black or hard swelling, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is abscess; and if it is declining with moisture, if it is spitting out pus, and there is a little spittle, and you deliver from both sides; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a broken glass vial until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished all the work; then lift the pale liquid easily and softly, and cure in other ways until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the throat apostemes.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes from the throat bones that are called "godath," and the pits have two almonds; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is abscesses of little sense and colour, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the discharge of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it is white in colour and the root is slender, if you have brought the instrument to cover it, but look first if the abscess is calm and peaceful.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fais seoir le malaide devant le soleil, et ses bras soient en ton sain, et il serre la bouche et prend les serjans entre ses mains, et presse la langue hors à tout l’instrument, de sorte qu’il soit formé; et soit d’argent ou d’argent subtil ausi comme un couteau.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, because this is the form; and let it be of silver or gold like a needle. Can you press the tongue against all this instrument? And you see the clot, take the sponge and hold it in the almond, and pull it out forcefully more than you wish; and do not take hold of any of the cloths with your hand, then close the instrument against the instrument, because this is the form, that seems like a force; and all the time the head is bent, and one place the other, and is very painful, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form: grasp one of the nipples with one tong, and the other with the other hand; and when you have grasped one nipple, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision and gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when blood appears, if you gargle the patient with hot water, or wash out grapes or millet, or similar things, until the wound is washed clean; then close the wound when it is healed. And never again will there be any other abscess in the throat except for the two nipples, if you grasp them just as you grasped the two nipples originally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and let his arms rest at his sides, and close his mouth and grasp the serjeants between his hands, and press his tongue outwards with all his might, so that it forms a circle; and let it be of silver or gold as fine as a knife.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so big that it had forced two stones out of its place twice.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had done so much, and remained in one place, I had bound the wound, then the fire went out, and in that fire I lost a great part of my bow; then I bound the other part in the other place where I did not wish to be, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I bound the wound in these abscesses, and I closed a part of it, and only a little blood escaped; and thus was undone the conduct of the woman from the throat, and now I begin to drink water and then wine, and I do not cease to tear at this wound for a long time; and the abscesses returned to their place, and filled up the body as much as I had eaten before; thus I embraced it and cauterized it within the throat: thus did the sense cross; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to me afterwards.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb hangs downwards, and it is escaping and is long, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is broad and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said before, and the remedy does not help, and you see that the wound has closed, and it is slight, if you must repeat the incisions; and that which is round and tight and is not long; and that is bloody or dark brown or black, if you must avoid the incision of the latter.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, from its pallor and its length, you must sit the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we mentioned before; then insert the ointment into the eye, and remove the discharge, and close with two sutures as I have said in the incision of the two almonds.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be known that you must not cover more than the superfluous which is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, you grieve the voice and the ear; and after the incision, use what we have said concerning the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, it must be known that you must use an engine for the cautery in the sense of fear.

li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The marks of an abscess are, as it is remembered from one thing and another in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which it is manifested, one of which is in its own likeness, and the other when it has moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And thus if it is for the limbs or if they are at the bone.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling at the head is different from that at the root, and the swelling at the bone is different from that which comes at the joints, and the nails have their own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there is swelling, one must not prick it until the bone is dead according to its degree; and if there are such things that one must prick it when it is stiff, and it does not die according to its degree, like swelling which is at the joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when swelling comes from the joints, and it is left as it is until it is bruised, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the opening is made at the principal part of the limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is middle-sized, it will go to the principal part of the limb; or if it is made at the foundation, if you do not pierce it immediately when it is middle-sized, it will cause swelling and fistula; and cannot be cured in a great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you wash the wound of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, when the pain has passed, and the departure of fever, and the calmness of the pain and redness, and the debate and tingling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and that you make the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and the place where it is painful; and that the perforation be long enough in relation to the abscess, and if the abscess is with hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and all the limbs or there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the limb itself.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the opening is in the flesh, if it is confirmed during digestion as we have said
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, if there is swelling of the limb from its venom, it is full of mud and dirt; and by chance it bites through the veins and penetrates the bone
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no wound that is perceived according to the large wound, according to what the limb has to bear.

Then the bone, and heal the wound as it is healed.
