en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In such a case as this, where you see a good arrangement of bones at the touch, and it is similar in color to bone, and is soft from one side and does not bleed from the artery or vein, nor is it deep; if you must break it, you must do so from below, and burn the soft part, and elevate the two levers of the forearm as we have mentioned in the apostemes of the head; and hold the thumb and index finger still so that you do not damage the nerve or vein, and do not cause swelling or bruising, except for the hand itself, and do not raise it too high before you have closed.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if thou copest the vein or artery, and this doth leave thee unable to work, if thou put in the wound a bit of vitriol broth or any powders that remain bloodless, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the swelling subsides, and soften the wound, and commence to move.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the swelling is gone, if thou return to thy work until it be finished; then when thou must indicate whether there remain any little scrofules, if thou copest them and grind them down.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is in the root of the swelling great blood, if thou canst not do anything but only cope that swelling at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging loose; then apply the wound of white cotton pressed with Egyptian balsam, and cure.</start_of_turn
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you remove all the superfluous tissue, if you gather the two layers of the wound, and close them now, there will be no further swelling due to the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if you understand to cover the root of the [disease] and drain away the pus, and close it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas which keep swelling, pierce them or they will die; and pierce them as before said, according to the circumstances, then mix with oil and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the oil cure has taken hold of the char, as long as it is sane.</start_of_turn
de squinance	When the limb has been restored and is stable, and all other parts are in their proper place, and there is no longer any swelling or pain, and the wound is not draining properly, then it is necessary to reduce the swelling and pain by applying counter-pressure.  This should be done by holding the limb firmly but gently with the thumb and index finger of the hand that is not injured, and by applying pressure with the thumb and index finger of the hand that is injured. This will reduce the swelling and pain and promote healing.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of the size of the gorge; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	As to those who have squinance, it is necessary that the epiglottis, which is called the 'fleshy tongue', be freed; and this will not help, for all the veins and blood vessels around the sick are at those which are placed high in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from the strangulation
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary therefore, when our wounds are about to burst the epiglottis, to cut them from three circles or four, a small incision through two circles or by the amount of the incision on the surface, not through the cartilage; and if it is necessary to join the epiglottis with the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the blood vessels are long enough.</start_of_turn
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the master is fearful, if you can, extend the skin of the throat to its utmost extent; then open the wound as far as it goes to the nail; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing; then close the wound as before; and demonstrate by the section of the nail that the spur will emerge from the broken bone, and by the hoarseness of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed and there is doubt of strangulation, gather the four limbs of the wound together, and bind them all around the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause the growth of hair, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The wound is deemed cured when the throat is fully healed, the patient is judged to be dead, and the default has vanished.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore close the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe; and he breathes through the wound; and thus is preserved from death; and for this reason the ancients command that the old man leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they command that the wound be closed and healed, until it is healed; and I shall tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a lady who had swallowed a knife, and lodged it in her throat; and part of the channels of her windpipe were broken. I hurried to call for help, and found her just like she was dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had escaped from it, and although it had not pierced any vein or artery except for the throat, it had bled excessively from the wound itself.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and closed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the lady did not feel any pain, and returned to her normal state; for in the handling of the epiglottis, I did not find any fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "neck hernia," and are great abscesses of a yellow color, and are very common in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is of two kinds: one is like butter to us, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not possible for me to do anything fierce except in the small one, and I prove and seek throughout the entire circumference: if you find it just like butter, and cannot reach any vein, if you touch it, as we touch the nose, and bring it out whole, if there is none; and encircle everything thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, until it is completely healed
des nous	And embrace all around, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of us are, of which I will speak of all; and behold that I tell you all the difference which is between health and sickness.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is caused by heat and fever that linger, until the swelling has subsided, and is accompanied by pain; therefore let the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With neither rest nor chill nor fever nor pain, and contains I saphus, which is his own sack and is according to the color of corn, and begins like fat and becomes large; and they are according to these signs, or grease, or moisture, and from the color are such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this, to first ask about the instrument called “enteromissor,” according to what its shape will be or what chapter it is in.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the inquiry of abscesses of us is that you take more moisture from the root than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs and fingers, until you know that the instruments have perceived the mark; then that it be according to the greatness of the abscess; then draw out the entrament, and take care that the spur does not bleed
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes too early, before the afterbirth has passed, and if the womb does not afterward bring forth moisture, if it is fat, then you must make an incision, and take hold with your fingers, and gently pull out from the navel; and if you do not cautiously pull it out, if you pull it out in pieces, nothing will remain.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, if it returns many times; if there is only a little left, and without grief, if you employ on the wound some corrosive powders, hold the wound steady, and apply soothing things around the wound, and cure it in other ways until it is healed; and if it is great, if you cut out two fingers of the wound, and cure what is causing the swelling.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If the vein swells up against you or something else forces you and if you use ground vitriol, and leave it for three days or two, until the wound has healed, and rest the bleeding; then return to cover what is left that remains damaged
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments used for cautery, and they are three in number: great, middle, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, for covering fistulas. And they are like needles which we sew wounds with, and they are made of citrine amber, or iron, or silver, and sometimes gold which are yellow, and they are more proven for black plasters for covering fistulas. And they are three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the forceps are like that of seeds, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and if the forceps have two curves of three kinds each; and if the forceps have three curves, and there are three kinds; and if the forceps have two curves, and a single curve only, and there are three kinds. And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of the humerus is fractured, and some have but one cut on one side, from which we draw the blood, for it does not clot from the vein or nerve; and from these introgressors are the bones renewed in pairs, so that the patient does not lose blood at the opening of the abscess; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and we use it only in the forearm, as in the leg and arm, and breastbone, and spleen, and in similar places; and no other instrument is ever used like these, resembling fists, according to this form, so that we staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one must never put it back into the place where it has already been closed with veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Blood does not swell in the breasts of many patients when they begin to fester, so that they seem like breasts of a woman; and they become heavy and limp, and those who see them will believe they are cured, if they are treated according to this form from line b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and use the medical dressing with charcoal, then join the two edges of the wound with stitches, and cure until it is healed; and if the wound leaks down, it is alleviated by its greatness as much as in women, if the pain is in two ribs below, by two similar incisions. When one is holding the other at the end of one and the other, so that the greater line contains the lesser according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the leather that is between the two edges, and break the fat, and bring together what we have said of stitches and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not quite finished, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the discharge of blood, if you must, fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive order. And leave it until it has eaten up the remaining fat and the wound, then cure until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of boils.</start_of_turn>
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come from the buttocks are managed by hard scrofula or if there are ribs, and there is only moisture inside.</start_of_turn
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	If there is moisture contained, it must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When any swelling is in the apostem, if one employs the wound of fine cotton, and leaves it until the other side, then bind up all the cotton, and cure the wound that comes from that as long as it is sound.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the apostem resembles carbuncles, if one does as we have said in cuts for carbuncles, and if the wound has entered the swelling, if necessary perform cautery as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de l’artere	From the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	If the artery is blocked, and the skin is swollen above, if there are many abscesses, or if the vein is burst and abscesses occur; if the surgeon knows that it is for the artery, if the abscesses are large enough to obstruct the passage of the hand; and if he knows that it is for the vein, if there is excessive bleeding around the edges; it is foolish to close this abscess, even if it has burst the testicles and caused swelling and pain in the groin and other parts of the body, and is great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to abandon the cautery treatment and the one who is in charge must also abandon it; in this one where there is an embolism of the artery that is under the skin for a long distance; then oversew the size as one would for needles, and take out the artery from the tissues until it is uncovered; then draw out from it a needle and pierce until the opposite side, and strain the artery with a doubled thread in two layers, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then pull the loop that is between the two links of an introversion until it is free from that which is in it, and rejoin the abscess; then administer the treatment that is adequate for the situation, until it is healed; and if the abscess is of the size of the vein, it is necessary to keep the hand in that position in which the abscess was made until the abscess is completely removed; then draw out the needle that you have in the hand and pierce, and there should be two doubled threads, so that you can handle it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have said, or tie with two parts of two threads that have two knots; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, you must insert another needle through all the threads from the beginning of the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in three layers; then cut the abscess as much as it is necessary, then cut the excess of the vein and leave that which is tied; then put on a wet bandage of wine and oil, and administer treatments of compresses and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Then put upon one drape of moist cloth in wine and oil, and mix with cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Then put upon one drape of moist cloth in wine and oil, and mix with cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often occurs in cases of attendants and those who must endure them or in all limbs where there are joints, and it is I grieve abscesses, and its colour seems like the colour of honey, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when it is strained, if it causes pain to the patient, it is not like honey, but like blood; and it swells very much from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, neither upwards or downwards, and that which is in the joints cannot be covered with iron: by chance there will be contraction; and he who is head or neck or brow, will burst the skin at the hairline.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have nails, hold them in its root; and if it is large, if you suspect bone, and burn, then fracture the bone and reunite the wound at the suture, and that is the cure as long as it is sound
des grosses boces pendans	When it is large, if it hangs at the edge, and is scorched, then bone it and reunite the wound at the suture; and heal as long as it is whole.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never have I seen such swellings elsewhere as in the belly; it is a disease which is called "funge" because of its resemblance to worms, and its root is subtle, and its head is large; and there are small and great ones. I have known of two bellies which appeared more like funguses than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were ulcerated at the bottom.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw two of them weighing respectively eighteen ounces and six and three-quarters, and the works in incision if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and has a thick root; if it comes to the large spatula and it is in your presence, order the fire cautery immediately.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the shoulder comes often too great discharge of blood, and if it does not go away, if you delay, then indeed burn it; and if you see the patient fainting and fearful of the incision of the flesh, take a good piece of silk thread and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then the restraint, and do not cease to drain the thread until it has held the joint, and ask of him work; and if the roots are tough, if there is fear at the bottom for the belly, but take hold of half, then burn it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep only that which is of dark color and poor sense and milk-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the cure of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the shoulder joint is inflamed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If a boil appears, it comes by burning of the wound or incision of the abscess, and is on the belly and there are some pus, as it happens in other ways, or blood that clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or swelling; and if it is through the abscess and through the issue of the bowel, if it is the color of the afterbirth resembling the color of cheese, and is a light thing with little pain, and opens with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the discharge of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with his two hands if it returns, and then comes back, and by chance if it is strangulated, and engulfs the mouth with the bath and for great work.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by moisture, it is a light matter; open it well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain me; and if it is by blood, if it is opened by these signs, the abscess is great and hard, and is filled according to a quantity; and if it is by wind, if it is blown upon the touch, and the work is that you must observe whether it appears to be by the blood of an artery or a vein, or the wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or in this chapter concerning abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If it appears to be by intestine or swelling, instruct the patient to hold his breath, and when he has exhaled completely, then mark around the swelling with your finger; then command him to grasp your hands together, and extend the limb that you have marked at all its joints; then pull the limb that is opposite to the swelling a quarter of its way; then bind it firmly with a strong thread or strong silk cord, and hold it in place; then uncover half of the swelling and place your index finger and the thumb over it; if you find the intestine caught in the binding, if you pull it out, let go of the swelling and bring the intestine back through the navel; if you find the swelling, if you grasp it at the navel and squeeze out the excess; if the artery opposes this, or the vein, if it is going well, then return to your work and take two needles, and pass two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have done in the shape that you think you will pierce; then strain the swelling for three days over the needles, and if you see that it is over, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it swells, and cut off the dead tissue by itself; or you can cauterize it when it is small and soft, and cure the limb of what is necessary, and keep the swelling as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and bandage the limb.
dou chancre	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of that which it comes, and bind the limb.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the signs of a boil, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how it should be avoided; and we say that a boil swells in the marrow, and has great caution in its cure, and that the old men say that when a boil is in the bone or can be pulled out like a boil that is in marrow, and in the flesh, and similar things, and that it must be removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is great and old, if you do not approach it, for I do not know that it can be cured; nor has anyone ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is in the bone or can be pulled out, as we have said, purge no more times the black bile; then make it healthy if there is obvious repletion; then remove the bile. That is to say, give a good drink of liquid to make the work; then draw out your ointments or boil, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts around nothing to leave; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb with your hand or with anything, and if it comes out contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize as much as you can without it being stained; then cure it of another cure until it is healed.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Nos avons dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et celle qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenchant from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And be trenchant from two parts, a point, and all the way through, so that it cannot be closed until it comes to the intestines when it is grasped, and cannot be stopped; then look if the dropsy is towards the intestines: if it is likely that you must make an incision three fingers’ breadth to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is for the disease of the liver, make your incision to the left of the navel; and if it is for the spleen, make it to the right, and do not make the wound deeper than the breadth of a nail or the thickness of an almond between the skin and the bone; then pierce through the skin with the instrument, and grasp the object, and keep your hand at the greatest extent between the skin and the bone, just as when grasping the quantity of an nail or an almond. Then pierce the bone as far as the thumb comes to the bone eight, and that is the mark of the water, then pull out the object, and there is your instrument.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, with a head of lead or barley lighter, and on the lower part there is a little hole; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other side, and one on the other side; and the head of the pin is cut off like a penknife. This is the form of incision which they write with the penknife.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the staple, if when the instruments are sharp they reach their peak, if at that moment the instrument is emptied, then immediately take out half or a third part, for if you take out more than that at that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will bleed, or he will approach death; but take out according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue for the patient signify, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the blood, which is now retained by the nail which is squeezing the hole that is above the socket, as I have said, that you pierce according to this method; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering in this way, and take out a small quantity of blood; do this neither way, and be careful not to use it until it stops bleeding.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and you see him spitting blood, if the physician treats the sepulture or sand burn, and by spitting or sweating or bath and sun, and remain thirsty; and the physician gives drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the blood, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the belly of the maiden.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark on their belly, or the mark is small, or it is not firmly in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If he persists so much that he does not perceive all that is around him very attentively, following this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or prick the soft flesh of the groin, and bind and hold it for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if he is kept closed, he will urinate and then return it; and by chance he cannot do this, because the urine that comes out will not leave him closed
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening of the wound is small, if it is treated with ointment of lead, as we have said, if it expands.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the wound does not bleed at its source, it is black, for no hair grows at the root that does not prick at its root until it has stretched out; and it cannot cover what is above without coming down to the marrow, which is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the shoulder and the scapula as wide as a thumb, if the mark pricks in the middle, as it should; and you keep from discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this blood which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils to the groin, and are an appearance of foul matter; and in them are malign and non-malign; if you take them at once [with a sharp instrument], one should anoint subtly, and cut and drain them all, then put on Egyptian lint; then cure with diafinicon until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is festering, of a bad colour and discharging pus, it is necessary to apply cautery to it.</start_of_turn>
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the wound is on the shoulder, and there is part inside the armpit and part outside, it is necessary to reset the wound that is inside first; and when it is healed, if the wound outside has healed.</start_of_turn
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure it altogether, if it is not firmly secured, the head of the shoulder will be perceived [as loose]; and blackness and corruption will ensue in its root or head; if you cover all that is black and corrupted, then apply above it a plaster made of honeycomb and flour, which is made from the peel of pomegranate seeds and sometimes, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bloodstained discharge comes, if you mix lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two arrangements together: that is, at the discharge of blood, and at corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you drink or force down hair a bundle of hair from the root, and the patient pisses among them; and when the hair comes loose from the root which has not been circumcised, or if there is wound or incision, if you then cauterize the circumference, as long as the ligament is untied, and deliver the head of the shoulder from all parts; and if it is necessary to divide this, if you cauterize it at the spleen and not at the head of the shoulder and the root; then dry thoroughly between them, and put on a bandage of linen moistened with cold water, which does not come loose.
de la circoncision	from the circumcision.</start_of_turn>
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of the other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and do it properly, if we are careful, it is the best work and the lightest to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us circumcision, for they did not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision in this way: with force and with a new instrument; but if the testicles escaped, because there were two layers, and by chance if we cut through these and left out that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Or the wound covers itself again, and there is double pain, and with the support which is too slight to secure the end of the limb; and by the support of the nail by chance escapes the thread, and straightens the work, and many times it is born again until it has no need of support and I want it.</start_of_turn>

dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from the obstruction of a stone, or blood clot, or bile, or barley, or other things which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not expelled, and you see that the obstruction is at the stone which is in the belly or the neck of the bladder, if it is possible that the patient is hunching over his knees; and let him put his feet on the back, extend his belly from the part below his back, and restrain the patient as much as he can; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is expelled; and if it does not come out, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible, administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes”; and this is the form: either of silver or lead shot like a sparrow; or the caine of a palm half long, or subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the method of extracting urine is as follows: if you take a double thread and tie one end to the chief of wool or cotton, and pass the thread through the tube; and press out the surplus of wool and pass until you reach the chief of the tube, then join the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair; and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moist and oily, and water tepid; then put the tube gently into the testicle, until it reaches the root of the testicle; then double the testicle towards the buttock; then pull out the tube before it reaches the bladder, and make the patient feel it come out until it is empty; this must not be done except in this order for that which it leads or goes is turned; then cut the thread at both ends and the urine will follow the thread, and withdraw it forcefully, and correct the urine; and repeat the tube until the bladder is empty, and be sure the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.

de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in this division about the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction with medicine; and I have mentioned the difference between a stone that is incarcerated like urine and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened of a certain size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and concisely about it.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is incarcerated in the bladder often causes vomiting, which is a sign that the stone is pressing on the bladder almost as much as in its entirety; and there is frequent vomiting, gravel in the urine, pain in the side, and many times the patient is unable to urinate, and then becomes constipated; and from these vomiting attacks the foundations are loosened.  The cure for these vomiting attacks is more gentle in young people than in old people, and is more effective in those between youth and old age; and the cure for those who have a large stone is more gentle than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	When we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient with a clustere, to remove all the dirt that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never happens that we must open the stone.
