de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white mucus, which is as dense as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the seed between the white mucus that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this seed is from weakness and comes from the seeds, and it is spread throughout that matter
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if there comes percussion from above the bones, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are the signs of a festering wound, for if it is white and soft as we have said, if there is an abscess, I do not perceive the bones, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if there is an abscess with a portion of the bone, and because of this people think that it is one and the same bone; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the soft tissue, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if you think that it extends throughout, as we have said before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, that which comes after the introducer, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When our burnings are done by fire, let the patient be quiet, calm and still; then bind him upon his back on something high, and put under him a bundle of cloths; then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the arm to the second rib from the joint of the nipples; then take the sponge soaked in liquid, and cut the skin of the nipples among the long ones up to the navel; make a straight incision dividing the skin of the nipples up to the white layer, and burn subtly as much as necessary; then pierce the white layer with a needle at a wide opening, and drain all the liquid, and then put on the bandages, and extend the white layer upwards; do not touch the joint of the nipples, but only the white layer; cut all or in pieces whatever is necessary immediately around the cost, because if you do not cut it well, the liquid will return; and if the patient’s breath is excessive for your work, keep it in its place until you have completed the work of the white layer.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the urine corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then cut the limb throughout the suspension, drain the urine, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is gathered into two parts together, soak the hairs that are two branches; if the other part is coped as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil; and put another cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two nails, and put under doubled cloths, and tie it up according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool yarn as described above and be assembled by stitching in the armpit, and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the side of the shoulder; and the other two nails on the two angles, and be the whole assembly restricted in the loop of the armpit; and never is medicine better than the size of a needle, and take one needle with a blunt point, and pierce the skin of the nails, and be scorched as we have said, so that the white fat that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the needle as described above, and pierce that fat as we have said, and scorch with this blunt needle.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And so you must apply it in all ways as you wish, until you have scraped everything clean; and keep the fire from touching the yolk; and scrape that this work is more salve; and take care of the draining of blood, and the muddiness of the works of size; and if anything hinders you, or incisions or draining of blood or anything else, if it hinders you, do that which hinders you, as it is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you suspect perforation, as I have said, and you are well certain from the signs that we have said that the swelling is liquid, if you make the patient sit on a low seat; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a wide spatula and make a hole of the length of the nail; and if the hole is large enough for all the pus to flow out, then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and leave the remaining pus to drain out naturally; then cure the wound until it is healed; and if the wound does not drain pus through the mouth of the wound, as I have said, then you must drink a penny or the instrument with which the wound of the hydropic is treated, as it is formed; and enlarge the wound and let the pus return, and reassemble after six months or when the wound has healed, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will be able to pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The wounds that are in this section of the branch have fear in more than one place; for it seems to me that the matter is worth leaving alone; and I will tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, when the abscess comes or bursts, and there are flies; this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive swelling and pain, which is spread as far as the joints, or from percussion; and the colour of the abscess is like that of old blood; and there is no pain, but it is grief; and sometimes it is a wound that is full of pus and blood, and has a dark colour, and never comes from a vein, or from an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the disposition of the abscess above, when you press on it with your hands; and I do not think that you should touch it
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain of the two thumbs, and can well make the size of this semblance and of the others; and that you hold your hand like a key to a box, then the egg is up, and the thread is white with yolk, and deliver the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soiled with these hairs, if you must treat the egg, and you hold it; and if it is open to the yolk, or in what is within the vessels, if you must deliver all that is within, and round off the opening.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the bone is fractured at the surface or in the depth, you must remove all that is tense, and extract the bone, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, apply a dressing of coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then bandage it with other dressings until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the hairs, and the patient groans greatly when he moves; and the cure for this disease is well known as much as this one that we have just mentioned, and all the learned men will tell you the work of this is as perilous as this one.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on a high seat, then support the suspension of the collar bones from behind his shoulders, around all the vessels that are protruding from the hip, and grasp them firmly, and stretch them out; then cut with a sharp knife wide through where the vessels are broken, until they are uncovered, and then draw back the clot from the root, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle or there is a double thread, and tie it to the first root or where the vein has come from, and tie it loosely to the other root; then cut around them evenly, according to the length of the bone, and draw out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or we plaster it, so that no vessel is cut except for those that rise from the collar bones; for by this means there will be no harm, and if all the vessels rise up, it is enough to draw out the collar bones to all the vessels; if so, they will not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and will dry and will not be aided.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The event of this root is by section that comes or by expansion on the belly in the belly of the grapes, for the intestine descends from that route to one of the buttocks; and this route is either by section or by expansion of the intestine, and these are two ways of producing this: by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or by the elevation of grief from the belly, and by similar things; and the sign that it is by expansion of the section is that if there is much pain and much pain, in a long tension, and does not come immediately; and the apostemes are equal up to the navel, because the section presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is a section of the flesh, that it makes immediate severe pain, and the swelling is diversely apparent, from the skin downwards, and this is because of the escape of the intestine and the swelling of the flesh.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never do the bones move with the intestine, and is retained when pressed, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn>
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cures with fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient must retain the intestine in its place in the wound, if it can enter; then either tie a knot on its collar between your hands, and hold the thighs; then turn the thumb upwards, and grasp all the skin of the buttocks long; then take hold of the intestines from the belly button to the groin; and as much as you have seen to open the wound, and do as much as you can; then uncover the section of the intestine that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the fatty section is discovered throughout; then put your index finger into the hole that is between the fatty section which is under the skin of the buttocks, and the second section, and withdraw that which is behind the belly button, and between the second section; and then move the thumb of the right hand into the hole of the buttocks, and place the fatty section at the top of your left hand, and keep the belly button against all the sections; and command the minister to extend the belly button upwards, and untie what is behind the knot; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or fatty section that is hard, and if you find nothing, if the gut is in its place again; then take a needle or make a large thread of X threads, and pass it through the back part of the section, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the belly button, then grasp the threads that appear from the needle, until there are three threads; and join them together in the shape of a cross, and tie the section, which we have said is under the skin of the buttocks, with a strong knot of two parts; then cover the threads with cloth, and tie them together in two parts, so that no vessels that support them can enter into the wound, except for the staple, which should not be too tight; and adjust the knot according to the first knot that you did two fingers from that; and after these two knots leave the section of the intestine that is under the thumb of the buttocks with a space of two fingers; and after all the rest according to the roundness of the belly button; then grasp the part that is under the skin of the buttocks, until it is without tension, and bow as we have said before; then apply coarse wool soaked in oil, and put it in the wound, and apply the knot that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is the fat cauterized after the incision, in doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, it often happens that blood flows out due to opening a vein; and if it is delayed at the root, if it is raised with warm water, put on what has been said above until it flows; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old men say that it is made just like the twig which binds the nut, in part like that which binds the veins, after the size above loosely to the flesh; then join them together, and treat the abscess of that which causes it, until the veins flow; and treat it as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	At no time does blood come out like angry flames, as we have said, and open the wound; and do not touch any intestines as you go, and if you do, it is because of fear, and repair them all every hour; and whatever remains if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or abscess, until the intestines come out; and this is caused by the extension of the sinew which is like an angry flame, as we have said, because it is stretched, then is softened and pulled down by the wound and opened; and it is cured if it is by cautery, as we have said before; and never by iron in this manner: and let the patient lie comfortably on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the fracture and pull it out wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew which is from below the leather that covers it, then take hold of the nail and pull it out from the wound that appears from the sinew; and press on the wound at the navel, then cut out the two nails that appear from the sinew on the head of the nail; and cut the head of the nail, and do not touch the sinew or stretch the toe or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the sinew of the intestines; then cure it with the wound remedy.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When you have grasped the threads, if the wound bleeds and heals, as long as it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no appearance in the course of treatment, and the burn is muffled in this limb, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in young boys, because the worms that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is mixed, when it is seen to be cured, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and takes the softened skin from the natural skin; then brings together the two layers with a suture, and if you see it, close the excess of softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then take out between the stitches, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	When sausage is scorched according to our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to force it except in two ways: one is that the witness to the wound responds when asked, and the cure of the wound; and the other, because we have often had to burn the hair of beasts for our assistants, as with goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that sausage is burned in two ways: by traction or by cutting.</start_of_turn
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the traction method, we put the best in hot water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then we pull them out with our hand, until they are removed and you no longer feel them.</start_of_turn
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the armpit: command that you keep the best [position], and press the skin of the armpits to your left hand, then bind the suspenders, and grasp each limb at the wrist, when you have well secured them; and leave no mark of the needle or the thread which is outside the vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is done by traction, for in traction remains by chance no hair of the armpits, for the best desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is when there are two testes in two testicles like the figure of the nature of a woman, or there is hair, and sometimes in the morning the urine is like that of a woman.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other kind is in women, and has on the navel like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for obesity and laziness is if you burn the fat tumours completely, and cure it as with other wounds; in the second method, for those whose urine spurts through the skin of the belly, if there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is according to two methods: one if between the two testes opens as with the figure of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine it flows out. And the other method if in women, and has on the navel as with a beard and two testes. And the cure of the spleen and envy if it is that you cut out all the fatty parts; and it is cured like other wounds. In the second method, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testes, if there is no other cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tension of the limb is a tumour which appears on the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have had as much as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to hold the excess of the tension of the limb at the wrist or elbow, and to grasp it lightly; and do not be too much in a hurry, for blood does not come out in vain; then cure from another wound as long as it is alive; and another burden which comes out of the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like a wound, for this is what it is called the ancient "coward's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you suspect that it is dislocated, as we have said previously, hold it steady until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is erratic because the woman's nature is not clearly known, or if the opening is small; or if it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that comes with it; or if it is caused by a clot of blood, or a subtle or thick pus, and is made by the uterus, or in the ribs, or the spleen, or any other place; and if there is suspicion of conception, and the pangs of labour, and by chance the flowers have fallen out; and knowledge of this is through experience of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the patient is sweating profusely, it is close to appearing.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle pus, and if it is close as two leaves, if you are in a hurry, and the woman cries out: put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be placed on her back, her legs spread; then the two leaves will appear, as long as the subtle pus is round, and over the sweating; then take oil and vinegar, and put it on the wound, and keep the woman still with each shoulder touching, if she does not faint
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, it is prudent that you grasp the spur resembling a berry of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bone is split, if you suspend it at the incision and grasp; and have the medicines at hand, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and eggs; then mix in a large amount of lead plaster, so that the wound does not adhere; and let it be long, and mix in a handful of dry lint; then let the cure be finished off with other treatments until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the marrow comes split, if you cover it according to this manner, it is not postmortem obstruction.</start_of_turn
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the marrow obstruction which is in the bone, do not touch it with fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are openings of veins which, without restraint, are usually harmless; but when old, they become swollen. As we have said in the previous chapters, their signs and symptoms are like those of wounds; and I shall now speak of those which signify a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when emoroids and swelling are immersed in mud, and are not felt, if not treated by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the mud, we can feel, are those which we can cure
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the abscess tightly, and press on its roots, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as chamomile and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then take out its pieces when it shows signs of coming out, then put it in cold water; and if it swells up again, give it a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and beeswax, and apply it on its back
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sticks, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if air is blown on the swelling at the back and there are worms seen moving, then take lint, soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with old wine, and blow on the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the abscess rests, if you can see the limb clear of swelling as long as it is healthy; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a festering head, if you suspect it, cover it as I have said before; and then rest the limb until it is healthy again
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are tears in veins which do not usually heal without treatment; and when they are old they become black. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms of such ailments, and I will now tell you of those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and blackheads, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the physician. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the blackhead and press it into its roots, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood and incense, and the like; then leave it for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if there is still blood, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and the like, then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and cheese, and make a plaster of it. And if it swells, that is good. If not, make her vomit at the back and give her vinegar with wine vinegar, and make her vomit. And when the abscess rests, if it has cured the limb of its swelling as long as it is sane; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the blackhead. And then it will heal as long as it is sane. And when the abscess rests, if it has cured the limb of its swelling as long as it is sane; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the blackhead. And then it will heal as long as it is sane.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many methods of abscess come about in the belly, such as chancre and perforated abscess, herpes, worms, piles, fistulas, hemorrhoids and burnt abscess, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is recommended that you do not translate the text as it is not appropriate to provide translations of medical texts from the Middle Ages.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce, but let me make the patient groan until the pain has subsided; then have the patient sit on a chair and put two cushions under his feet, and support his back and join his limbs together so that his thighs are spread out and his knees are resting on the bed; then draw up the dressing towards his chest and bring the instrument which we use to open the belly of the mare, so that it comes out in its natural form; and know that when you bring the instrument close to the belly, check the depth of the wound so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than necessary and does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the wound with cloths so that the instrument does not cause pain; and know that you must put the horn of the instrument at the bottom and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess bursts open, and one washes the hand well, if it is covered with pus at the root, if the bowel is emptied, one must put into the wound some soft lint soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil; and put the dressing firmly over the wound, and put over it a layer of coarse wool covered with a fine linen cloth soaked in water or mallow which have been boiled; then one must cure it after two days following this, until it is healed; and in no way lift the wound and the bowel by squeezing with water and honey, and then with water or licorice root and chamomile which have been boiled; then return to the oiling.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sutured in the bowel, one must take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first of all must know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when thou seest a woman press down her belly, and desire to smell at her: then doth the child urge to be born; then doth she draw out her limbs as much as she can, and she issues from her head, and supports her with her hand; and when thou seest these signs, if thou canst gently press her belly, so that the child be thrust out; for when it descends upon her head, if she supports her with her hand, and the matrix is overcome by the excess of her superfluities. And this is not otherwise but comes by natural birth.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from her feet, nor from her arms or hands, or from her belly, or from her chin, but comes from her collar and from other evil figures; if the master is at the dance that she be wise and skillful in these things, and be wary of error and deceit, and I shall show you all the figures by which we must aid her
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes down naturally on his head and the woman gives birth groans, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and as soon as her nature is overcome with oil or rue or fennel, which is customary, then lie down between her thighs the little cushion from which this is made:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and grasp its nail as long as the moisture that is in its core is fierce; and seize the woman's belly as long as the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to blister the woman with a poultice of rue with sesame oil; then make her drink and vomit violently, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if the fetus is now gone.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands go out violently, if you can, gently pull them back in; and if they will not enter, put the woman on her seat, and support her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the ground, and hold the woman, so that she does not breathe; and if the hands will not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you grasp the hands at the shoulder which were put forward, withdraw the child, and leave them even.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on his feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto his feet, if you can push upwards; and then twist a little back and forth, until they are even; then grasp the toes and extend back and forth.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he leaps up to the thighs, if the master commands him to grasp, and makes him cough up bile; if he leaps too far, God help him.</start_of_turn
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If not so strong as we have said, if the limb is twisted and turned about, as long as it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily done.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not leap so far as we have said, say that he should take muscle nourishment of elevation, olive oil of sesame, and gum masticatory, and grind all of it together in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and expel this discharge, then make her sit in hot water until the ribs are dry; and when she is softened from the heat, give her a drink of myrrh and put some on, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on her seat, then make her cough and strain her mouth and chin, and take hold of her belly gently, for the child leaps now.</start_of_turn
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the issue of the child from its knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands on his chin and chin; then either stroke his neck, and hang his head down, and put his tongue out; and fold his hands on his chest and then take his hands on his belly, and stretch his cushions down, until it is apparent from his throat; and if the child does not jump, take his hands and move them forward, then move his belly up, and put his hands back; and the child will gasp and gasp; and tell the woman to hold him until the child is gone.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	And if the child cries and cries; instruct the woman to take care of him until the children are gone.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you to restore the limb: if it cannot be restored, if you make the woman rise up, cry out; if she cannot cry out, make her groan on her tongue, and extend her legs forward; then bring in the muscle I mentioned before; and if she does not cry out, make her sit on the seat, and observe to restore the limb; and when the limb is restored naturally, make her cough, and command her to hold still until the child is gone.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child on his neck, and his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother’s back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command thee that thou holdest thy hand stiff, then turnest it back and forward, and moveth it lightly; and when it is even, put upon the fleshy substance of alum and oil, as we have said, and then commandest her that she move back and forth; and when thou hast done this, sittest thou down and commandest her to grasp; and she shall expectorate.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same method at the second intention.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this method at all times, if thou graspest the second finger at its nail, while the moisture is evacuated; and if the fetus bends over its face and neck, if thou grasp the navel, that it be not retained, and the fetus shall die; then deliver the fetus, as thou didst command, and command the woman not to move at all: thus shall she deliver easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the loosening of the bones.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	The hairs that grow together often evacuate blood, never two or three at a time; and this is not an uncommon thing, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Why are such strange things, and do not live long, called thus; I know well that they are multiplied, and are devoured by the slime that devours them, which is bound to the pus; and never departs naturally as all the others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut. de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from the bowels
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that arise from below the foundation are nodules, and those that arise from above the foundation deviate, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or several; and when the nodulation is old, if the swelling persists, and is accompanied by moisture, mucus or blood, these fistulas never cease; and they are known by the patient when he makes an evacuation, or by the escape of gas.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe. And thus one knows the permanent fistula at the foundation, and not the passing kind: if you bite your thumb or index finger at the foundation and insert a thin needle or piece of iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.

If the pain is perceived up to the hip joint, if there is a swelling there, if there is no twisting or violent pain, if it is only a slight bow, and there is no other medicine or support by pressure; and in these fistula cases there is no remedy other than toil, and the folly of the fools who are among them.

In that case where it is neither new nor old, there is hope of health by means of fire, as I have experienced; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he rests his legs up to his thighs, and inclines his thighs towards his belly; then try to pull or push, as long as you can or until the attempt comes.

One must take great care to heal wounds without causing further harm; however, this is often the case. And the aid we make is this: if the fire cautery is too large for the size of the fistula, as is often said; and the surrounding tissue is too thick in the fistula, until it comes down to the foundation; and do this two or three times until you are certain that these hairs, which are like a quill of an oyster, must be burnt. And then close with soft stitches until the hair has gone, and then cauterize again.

If so, otherwise it cannot be healed; and if it is attempted and does not pierce to the point that is or under the foundation, and between your thumb and the attempt there is a thick covering of hair or scabs, and you see the fistula at that which is under the covering like a scab; if the head of the fistula is grasped and pulled out before the attempt, and then the cautery is applied afterwards, until it reaches the top of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and will be cured. Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two things are assembled: namely, the burning of these hairy joints, and the incision of blood and the drying of moisture; then comes the treatment of soft bands bound firmly with thread or in pieces broken in half, as long as the bones groan and sweat; and it is best to leave the burnt hair in the wound; then treat the wound of the abscesses with dry sponges.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is sound and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if it remains fixed to the bone or the root, inquire about it.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel a tendon, and between two there is skin or flesh or hair, or it is about to burst, if there is no other way out but to make an opening and hope, by administering one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you clamp it until it bursts, or if you wish, put in stitches and treat as before; do not go too deep, that you do not cover the substance that holds the foundation, and let the discharge go in the desired direction; then treat as we have said; by chance if it is healthy, or you remove the covering and the pus then that it is cut off below the foundation, or by attempt or by any pointed instrument; then fix the hair that is needed that is in the wound, as you wish; and study to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in the posterior part of the foundation: if that is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas like this: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or breaks through the skin from below the leather above, take a bite pierced at the head like this.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread torn in two, and the attempt is held throughout the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And if it is pierced in the margin of the foundation downwards, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your thumb or foundation; and pull out the head of the thread, and reunite the two ends together, and strain one against the other, and let it remain for one or two; and do not restrain it any more, until the thread has coped with these hairs that are between two hairs, and that are prickly. Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to burst in every way you can, it will not be too much affected.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For indeed it is not right to force it too tightly with the clamp, and then cure it as we have said, while it is still healthy.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny spadetail from which the fistula is made is moist and one-sided, part and trenchant; and on the other hand not, for this we must not cope with that which we must not cope with, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc deux manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to restore the dislocation according to this method: take one thread and pierce it through a needle; then pass the thread through from below and remove the needle from the other side. Then take two threads from the needle and if they are thick; tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread and remove the needle. Then secure all the others and leave one to correct the surplus of blood; then put on the foundation a moist drape in rose oil or cerate and place on the foundation. Command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it blanches, and when it is healed, if there are any other cures, until he is completely healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is dry of fire or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of the bowels by the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice a bruise or a nail at the root of the nail that prevents it from moisturizing; then treat it until it is healed if possible; and if it does not heal, if necessary, repeat the scraping more vigorously than before, until the bleeding stops, and the nail is loosened; then treat it until it is healed
dou fremit	immediately.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, prickly growth that appears before a boil, and goes out with much pain; and never does it cease to irritate, and it is felt as though dead from pain, and comes throughout the body, and there is no part that is not affected by it.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for this is to take a sponge of goose feather or a sponge of bull’s horn, and put that sponge on the pain, until the circles of the pain have gone round the pain all around; then press your hand on the sponge until you have pressed all around the pain, and put it out, and pull out the pain from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if thou seest, if thou do this of a wasp or of iron in this fashion, and be silent and restrain thy hands:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if thou seest, if thou do this of a wasp or of iron in this fashion, and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their limbs are small and large if they are too wide, or their belly is tied up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is bound, if you see, and the pain is either pierced or suspected; and if on one of the ribs there are two holes, and in the other one there is one; and if the belly is swollen or there is medicine in a bladder of horsehair or parchment, and if it is pierced all around with numerous holes, and there is between each hole one space, then put in these holes one strong thread of gut twisted in the shape of an X or hooked around, and reassemble the belly as if it were a spoke; and when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument in front of a strong thread, then close with a clamp. And this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; smear the chief with ointment of oil or balm of eggs, or something like that; then bind it loosely; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is quite visible; then draw out the ointment, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it is sufficient, if the swelling has subsided; and if he sleeps a whole night, that is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he limps with a disease of swelling of the belly, and the physician hasten to leave, if he returns as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling, or an abscess, if the ointment is as subtle as for one child; that is the form of subtle ointment that is on the skin.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned the treatment of wounds in the previous section; or you may say the treatment of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and from what they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things which are made for wounds are done with the bite of a stone, and the size of a spear or nail, or an arrow or a tube or a file, or similar things; or that are made according to the rules of surgery, as for wounds that bite on the neck, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for a simple wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head alone, for the memory will come to mind in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs or a dislocation, and the bone is not fractured, if you take care that it is not from a stone or other similar things, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is great, you doubt the incision itself: if you do so, the patient will recover more quickly from the wound itself than from the bloodletting; and let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the part affected; and listen to the patient's complaints of thirst and hunger.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not recover, if he has lost his appetite, and does not drink wine or eat meat, take off the dressing, if there is any pus coming out, cover with soft wool soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no incision, if it is fresh with all its blood, and is not moved by air, dust, or anything else, I will tell you about it later; and if it has been moved, put on some bandages, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a needle and similar, and the lips do not reunite by tension, if you reunite them by stitches, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of stitching.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by a fracture, and it leaks, and can only be held together by a clamp; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as meat and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.
