And if you find or leather rotting, and there is no fracture, if you clamp it tightly, and let it bleed, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched by medicines, if it is an artery, and if you find it dislocated, if you bind it with a thread; if this does not help, if you cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if the cure is light: then put on this powder which hardens as soon as it is moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and powder them finely, and apply them to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it is well closed and reunited with all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for we do not oil the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Never do we make this treatment solely, when there is neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.</br
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if one does not put on this powder; but put on some unguents digested, or poulps of coarse flour made of water and honey, until it has healed; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture accompanies the wound, and it is small, if you extract the fragments cautiously; and I will tell you about large fractures later.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	Wound comes from a tear and is simple, if there is no difference between the root and the top of the limb, but if the root or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, if there is no other ailment except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, because it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; and do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most delicate part of the body; but if the medicine is strong, like molten chalk in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and ivy leaves washed in sweet water, and other stones of this kind, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, if the pulse and veins are tied, then treat until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and swollen, with much pus, if the wound is pierced or lower down the limb; if the artery is severed, blood flows freely; if the bone is fractured, the marrow and the cautery mingle; if the wisdom tooth is pierced, or the cheek, and the tongue is held, because the meat hangs there; and then tighten the wound gradually, and leave it alone for a while, then cure it with ointment until it is healed; if the wound has made an impression in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments are numerous, do not attempt to remove them all; leave as many as possible, and let the wound heal naturally; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the cure is like I have said in the chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of wound by lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if you see that the wound breaks the wind, that is to say that it is deadly; and if it is not deep and is fresh throughout, if you do not put in at the first hour the powder, do not bind it up with the wound that it does not cause further pain or swelling; remove the dressing and give the patient rest; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice; if you do not have an astringent, put in the wound some coarse cotton to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep over the wound for three days, or four or more; if there is no spasm, do not move or strain the limb. When you see the bones in their place, that is to say that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tension of the tendons and other cures, as long as he is sane; and if it cannot heal, and if it is necessary, remove the bones that have fistula; as the treatment requires.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or a knife, and it is simple, or high up or at the back, if the treatment of what is before is necessary; if it is large, suture it; if it is small, dust it off, and if it is embedded in the bone, and pieces are broken off, if desired, remove the wound, and drain the pus if it is purulent; and if it is not purulent, leave it open, if it aligns with the extraction of the bone fragments.
dou derrompement dou ventre	dou derrompement du ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The swelling of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound never does the intestine protrude, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the introduction of blood; and the suture is more painful, and never is better than a small wound than a great one, because it brings back the intestines more promptly, if they are not brought back piecemeal; for the intestines swell so much that they feel the pain, if they are brought back piecemeal, and for this reason is better the lesser wound, because it brings back the intestine to its place as well as other things. And bones that have burst through the belly are according to four methods: the two common sutures come together in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the flesh and two other sutures are common to other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say a word and declare
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and all other things are relaxed, two methods may be used: or by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area slightly: moisten a sponge or lay a wet cloth on it only, or pour on in boiling water squinching and scraping, and draw out the intestine as much as the swelling allows; and never do this without first restraining it, for it is useless to do so when the swelling has subsided.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is moist with water or elevated and cooked badly, for by this means the entrance is aligned with the things; and if it cannot enter, if make an opening at the edge of the wound with the instrument of grasping, for it is better to grasp the blood clots; and the first treatment is useless if the wound is large, for no more should be cut than is absolutely necessary. This is the instrument for cutting: if it runs into the curve and escapes not, and if this is the shape:</start_of_turn
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude outwards, if you stop the bleeding in accordance with the natural form in its own place, be aware, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and is in the lower part of the abdomen, if you must manage the patient on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and if the intestines are protruding from the belly, if you put one hand on the navel and the other on the hip, and if the lower part of the belly is in one of the two lower parts, put your thumb on what is above so that the higher part is greater; and in this way you must prevent what I say about large and soft wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, put what has appeared between your hands, and take hold of all the edges; and this is the common way of stitching, and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound, then leave a space at the head of the wound and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is from the inside of the skin, until you have pierced through that part, and assemble the two heads of the needle together; then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, then assemble the two holes of the wound together, and then leave a space, and pierce another needle; and tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing this until the wound is completely held together; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles will not hold all the flesh, and the thick ones will not penetrate well; for this reason you must make them moderate; do not push the needles too far from the flesh and the skin, as they will not hold and will open the wound before the stitching is finished; and then pull the threads together so that they do not bleed the patient at night, and put patches or bandages over the holes of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them in place until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because there is only one needle or two at most for the second stitching, and that you assemble the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the needle together with one needle or a strong thread in the middle. And when you have pierced these three holes together, remember the needle at the part where you began, in the manner in which we cut the threads; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a small thumb; this stitch will hold the flesh, and I stitched a wound once for a wound which was made by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of a hand in size, and there were intestines well two palms of great size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will return the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound will be closed after fifteen days. The cure was successful and the patient recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he had judged that it would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat it with any medicine, for I was in Italy where there was none to be had, neither medicine; and the treatment was simply to apply pressure to the wound twice a day, and to bathe it in honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two ways to stitch: take the needle and pass it from the underside to the top of the wound until you have grasped the right corner; when it has grasped the right edge, if you have slipped the needle or if you have passed the needle too close, and you have pierced from the underside once more, and you make it pierce from the other side of the wound until you have reached the underside; and you understand this stitching if you stitch just as the cobbler does with leather, and that you leave one lip of the wound open, and you start again from the other, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with great care, if it is done without violence, which joins the two parts naturally, and brings one chief close to the other chief, in this manner: pierce with a needle or the chief of a nearby splinter, and pierce only the lower part, and leave the two chiefs of the splinter; then withdraw the needle, and pierce from the lower part until it reaches the centre, having two chiefs of the splinter; then pierce one and the other from the lower part until it reaches the centre, in two other splinters which are on the other side; and this is the wisest method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens said concerning this matter, and no one testifies, we must sew up the belly with two needles, or there is thread in the cheek; and one needle must be pushed in from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew up wounds; and it is safer when the gut is in the middle of the belly than when the stitching is too tight for the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the cost, then put on the nourishing powder and char; if it has moved, do not put on any other dressing than is present, until the wound is healed; then tighten the thread and sow the skin, the fat, and the membrane; then cure the wound like the others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, simply put on a dry dressing and let it clot twice as much as is necessary until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You do not need any other medicine in many cases of wounds except for simple ones; and if you doubt that the wound does not cause common disease in the principal members, you must moisten coarse linen with warm olive oil or rose oil, and put it around the abscesses, and drain the boils; and if it feels pain or gangrene in the bowels, and it happens many times, if the black vomit comes up, and in the same way if the gangrene comes up as far as the intestines; and pierce the belly, and drain the abscesses as soon as when the large intestines are more lightly affected to heal than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, for it is because of the swelling of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and for the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the liver bursts from a wound, if you return it to its place while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black, if you tie the black part, since there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the liver and the spleen, and hang the two arms down from the lower part of the wound until the bursting has subsided, so that the extraction is aligned when the liver bursts, and the wound contracts.</start_of_turn>
de la routure dou boueil	Of the root of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in little pieces, for I have seen that one bone has burst from a wound or the belly of a lance; and the wound was at the stomach, and became filled and became a fistula, and in this there was evacuation and vomiting; I cured it according to what I could, and I did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the limb was straightened.</start_of_turn>
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has any harm in his belly; and there is no harm, but a great improvement, and food and drink; and they say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be closed in parts. Take tweezers and grasp the lips of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the mouth, if it has grasped the mouth above; then pull the tongue, and this will suffice if it does not slip, and put another tweezers after in the same manner as before, until the wound is whole; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is burned in the intestines, and there is no nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a fine silk thread which is cut from the intestines of a beast, in parts. Take the head of this silk intestine which is already detached, and then ligate to the head of this silk one thread of fine silk twisted, and pass the thread through the needle, and suture the intestine, and keep it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce except according to the way of love and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, as it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no danger or infection, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds that arise from any wound or incision, when they break open, if called throughout 'fistula', and indeed even when they are closed and rent bowe.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to truth a nodation that must be firm and white, or where there is no pain, and is just as closed as the quill of a bird; and never in clear broth, and sometimes thick; never thin, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is pus, is only by one of the seven causes: namely, by the smallness of the wound or its hardness; or by its malice; or because there is hardness within, and upon the skin, that does not allow pus to grow; or there is too much discharge; or the flesh is rigid, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property of the region is tardy in digestion and in health, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone: and I have already mentioned all these causes, and their signs, and their cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or I must tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that arise in all members with pain; for there are wounds that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or the intestine, or the bladder, or at some of the bones, or at the spinous process of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet; and if part comes to the property of the main limb, and the rest.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All wounds of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no wound that does not reach the marrow except as I have said, and you have betrothed a cure, and you see it proceeding, if a vein or an artery is pierced, because the clot will be formed in the twisting; and if the wound is deep, if the clot of a subtle attempt to draw it out, for the clot will swell around the twisting; and if the wound is perforated and you do not well cover it with attempts, if it bursts by one of the perforations, for the moisture is too short from one perforation to the other, and it softens; then you must know well the bone or the nerve that is broken, and if it is sheared off, and ask the patient about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or in some of the things that I have told you, if the fracture agrees with what I have told you, and if the bone is fractured, and the corrupt pieces that are within; then the cure as long as it is not healed, and if the wound is well perforated from the right side, if you can cope as you wish, then put soft tests in medicine ague, and keep them until the medicine consumes the superfluous that is remaining at the bottom; and then put oily unguents around the wound, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is fractured by the wound, if you can cope.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or major arteries are not obstructed, neither the bones nor the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is broken, and there is corruption and blackness, if the marrow is whole as long as the corruption is of bone only, then heal the fractured bones with warming compresses until they are healed; and if they are not healed, bend them as before, extract the bone fragments until they are gone; if the fracture is complete, and when it is completely healed, restore the limb to its original position.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, extract the fragments of bone which are too deeply embedded; do not attempt anything further; if there is nothing else to do but let things take their course; and if there is only a small fragment of bone which can be easily removed, grasp it with appropriate forceps, and if there is any larger fragment, remove it whole; do not leave any fragments behind. If moisture opposes you, and there is no fear of death, use pressure and moisture and warmth, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not remove them at an opportune hour, if you place over the wound some substance that causes putrefaction, and leave it until the wound is surrounded by bones, then in this case you will have less pain in the bones. And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, if you pull out the corruption as much as possible until the marrow is entirely exposed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the bone that is corrupted, and you bring it down to the level of the bone, if you cover it with lint and cover all until the corruption is gone, and then cure it until it is healed; and I tell you of a fistula that happened to me in my leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There once was a young man about the age of thirty who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, until the matter came to the leg, and he fled from a large abscess that occurred without any known cause; but he remained foolishly occupied with the abscess above all else, and corrupted a great amount of matter, and a fistula formed, and there came out so much pus that all the bones creaked and the matter of the bone was moist; and he remained like this for two years, and there was no knowledge in his hands, until I was called there, and I saw his leg and the medicines he was given, and what cured him of the fistula.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound one of these holes with a loop, and then I encircled all the holes, and I found that one followed the other throughout the whole limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I bound one of these holes with a loop, and then I pierced it until I discovered a piece of bone, which was corrupted and slimy, and it continued to be corrupted right up to the marrow; I soothed that which appeared to be corrupted bone, and I thought there was no further corruption except for that which I had seen; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines, but I could not close it; and I repeated the process, and once again I discovered the corruption continuing in the bone, and I soothed it, and then I left it alone, and I thought I would try to close the wound; but I could only do so as long as I grasped a part of the bone, and I had to remove it entirely, and then I restored it with medicines; and it healed completely and was closed without any further recurrence, except for the weakness of the patient, who was unable to endure the pain, and for fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is blood evacuated thereby, but the patient remained entirely sound, and there sprang from the bone a hard scale, and it was in good condition and did not cause any inconvenience or any discord to all, neither to the spirit nor to the body, neither to the spirit nor to the body.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the limb, if you must bind it in this manner: take one thread and stretch it at the head of the bone which breaks, and command no one to lengthen it upwards; and put another thread of linen thicker than the first one on the other side of the bone, and bind it over the scale which is detached from the bone, and stretch the head, so that you tear the corrupt scale away from the bone, and uncover the scale on the limb or where you see it is bound; and put a cushion or a piece of gauze under the bone to cover the corrupt scale, and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or a part, uncover the marrow all around; then put on the thumb and index finger, and join the corruption from one part to the other; and be certain to join for the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, if you join the corrupted joint and join the bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other angle except that of the cover; and if the corruption is at the wrist or the elbow, if it is very strong in that thing, but in any case you must inquire about the corrosion, how it opened; and moderate it in all the ways you can, but that the vein or nerve does not suffer from it; and that the incision and sutures cover these bones many times, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of pus, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to consider the resemblance of the work to its instrument; and that the work will show you the instrument which you must have, according to your knowledge of this art and the testimony of the manners of diseases; if you are uncertain of the instrument which you must have according to this, it is necessary to inquire about it.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder is dislocated by moisture, by pressure, or by violence. When you have treated the cause of the dislocation with medicines, and it has not healed, if you do not cover that limb until the cause has passed, the patient will either escape from death or from the malice which is greater, the default of the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards comes the blackness, because that corruption of the limb spreads throughout the limb and takes hold of the whole body. If you delay covering it, and if this is caused by the percussion of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea, vipers and the like, if the corruption is at the root of the shoulder, and you do not give it space to come out, until it reaches the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, if the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it goes beyond the elbow, it is death, and there is no stronger remedy than the quantity of its virtue; and all in all that is done when the corruption comes or returns: if it comes in the first joint, if the cope afterwards comes in the second joint; and if it comes or returns, if the cope is throughout; and if it comes in the leg, if the cope is at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, there is no other remedy but that the patient should die; and to cover the limb with a cloth or bandage if you bind it below and above, and stretch one minister from the lower lip of the jaw to the other minister from the upper lip, and you separate the cartilage that is between the two lips to the width of a spatula, until the bone is exposed; then cope or remove the bandage, and put a bandage on the part where the cloth was, so that the bandage does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient other lesions and incisions.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb too much, or if you put on restrictive powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied by something; then bind the limb securely with a strong bandage, and treat until it is healed; and I will tell you that in this house there was a man with a black spot that seemed to burn, and that corrosion began in his palm, as it burst all the bones; and when we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the bone, he was healed; and long after the corrosion had gone, the palm returned, and it came to me, and I put on protective things after the inflammation of the sore, and I could not stop the corrosion; and I advised him to cut off his hand, and I did not want to give him any hope of recovering the matter; and I doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the strength of the body was weak; and he awoke, and returned to his home, and he covered his hand, and he was healed; and I have never heard of anything like it except for this, when we have been forced to do it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes abscess in flesh without swelling; it remains so long as it makes great assembly of blood; then it breaks and bursts, and in leaping up the blood, it bursts the vessel; and the skin which is under is as delicate as a silken cloth, and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so elongated that it reaches the bone embedded in the marrow, it is called "fistula"; and the skin if you cut that skin entirely, and even when it is delicate, is like a silken cloth; and it does not return to its former state.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect that the skin is taut and that the corruption is not in the marrow, and the skin is thick as horn, in such a case do this: look if the swelling is great and if the blood in it has a foul odor, then make a blister of Egyptian medicine which is to be made thus: take equal parts of alum, oil, and alum, and mix them together; put the mixture in a vessel over a fire, until the medicine is red and thick like honey; then take some of this according to your need, and make a plaster of it, and bind the area; leave the plaster on for two hours, then take it off while expressing it out; do this several times until the swelling is reduced and the pain is gone; do not use alum of tartar, except when this medicine is not present, for take tartar from the bottom of a grapevine, and let the liquid drain out, then mix in the alum, until you feel that the swelling is gone; if the patient cannot bear the pain, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the alum of tartar will help; or if you mix alum with honey or if there is a little bit of alum in the plaster.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is in parts, if you do not leave it to swell, if you do not cover its sides as you see, it appears in such a manner that the bow goes down lower than it is; for when the bow is in parts, if you do not leave it to swell and if you do not cover its sides as you see, it appears in this way: that the bow goes easily forward, and leaves nothing of the bow; and take consolidating medicines to bring out the blood, and extend over a drape of linen that covers the whole wound; then close the forces where the hole was made more widely than before, because there are often soft things on the other drape following the quantity of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to align the bow, and do not remove the great drape until after one time; and that which is outside the hole, often removes the bow, and its discharge is what corrects the bow, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digested or indigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine is in this way extended and you see the nature that leaps upon the hole of the wound, if its discharge has already occurred, and approach the health; and then take off the dressing in the morning or the third day, and when you take off the dressing, if there is change in the other drape, renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it still bleeds profusely after the third day, soak the wound so that the blood does not clot further.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle pain comes suddenly after a long tension, if you do not quickly recover your senses, for your life is approaching its end.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those who delay their wounds by eating flesh in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if they become unwell after prolonged lying down, their veins swell up and do not shrink; and if they rise too quickly, they are prostrated, because there is too much moisture in their body. Therefore, if there is excessive moisture in the body, it is necessary to take purgatives of both kinds, such as rue heliotropium and rhubarb; and aloes with vinegar and oil of roses; and use them with honey. Because there is much vitriol in this; and this is the last medicine. Take rue heliotropium and make a decoction with rose oil and vinegar equal in quantity; then filter and use. This will cause the boils to swell and discharge pus, when the purgatives are not present. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the incision of the abscess.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess which arises from the swelling of a pouch of the hand, or the foot, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is envious, and one does not take care, if it comes there will be a running abscess, and it will break and discharge pus until it reaches the root of the swelling, and by chance it will break all the way; and there comes the corruption up to the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the abscess is large, and the color is yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have cured it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, if you must, you must cut away all the excess that remains of the swelling, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the swelling is soft; and if the swelling is pressing on the nerve, and it begins to swell, and to bleed, if you must, put on the root of the swelling the right amount of cautery to stop the bleeding, and the pus that is above, and gently cut away that part of the swelling that is superfluous, and put on the remaining part of the swelling medicines that are astringent and corrosive to destroy all that remains; then let the wound heal until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise. la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand comes from the wrist.

des vils	Des vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The hairs are black and cover the body like dark fat, full of melancholy humours that come in abundance to many limbs with pain; and more often they arise from those who walk and work and bear burdens, than from others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give any purgatives, and then repeat the poultice.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment for fire is in two ways: one is with vinegar, and one must force out the black blood; or the other method is that you cauterize the vein, and you must force out all the blood.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first grasp the limb firmly and do not weaken it, then strain the limb of the patient from under the shoulder down to the part just below the knee; then cut the vein in one, or two, or three places, of a large size, then close and force out the black blood from your hand, from the tip to the thumb, until as much blood has drained as the patient can tolerate; and then close the wound and command the patient to eat flesh with black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it will be harmful to the patient.</start_of_turn
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The ailments of the limb are thus: open the limb of the patient, if there be hair, then put or bathe it in hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, if the patient is able to bear the heat of the fire, then burn the hair at the root of the limb, or in the part below the ankle; then cover the skin with ointment, and press the limb from the ankle downwards until it feels relaxed; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white thread; then remove the hair from below, until it is freed from the skin, and then apply ointment lightly, and press it in another place nearby; then burn another size, or several if necessary, and when you have finished, remove the hair from the root and draw it out, until it is all gone; and if you do not manage to draw it out and it remains firmly embedded, then there is a splinter at the end of the hair, and you must grasp and draw it out, and there will be blood at the root, and wipe your hand with a part and with the other, until it is gone; and keep it still, for if you move it, you will not be able to draw it out or lift it, and this will cause harm to the patient; and when you have finished, put out the limb of the wound with clean wool and oil of roses and cure it until it is healed.

When the opening is made, if you suspect that the surrounding area is too soft, surround with a piece of sponge from one and a half inches to two and a half inches thick, and hold in place, and leave the sponge in the limb until it is all the way out; for if you pull out the sponge, if it enters the flesh, it brings about an abscess or gangrene or death. Therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and thoroughly from the very beginning, and that nothing be left or remain within; for I have known of cases where this vein has been treated with five palms of sponge, or ten, and one hon has come out to me from ten palms of length, and when it was pulled out, there was one wound or hole in the flesh, and all was lost.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens in the elbow or on the wrist, and it comes from bursting blood; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo sickness," because it often causes spitting, and is a small vein that grows between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, upwards and downwards, and causes pain all along the limbs until it reaches the skin or breaks, and spurts blood; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, worms, and pus or belly-ache; and it is dangerous because when it runs through the body, and rises to the head, and comes out, by chance it returns and destroys the marrow.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture. This ailment is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the joints, and since it moves from joint to joint; I have seen that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to visit a sick woman, and discovered swelling on her arm, and I saw a small swelling in her armpit; and I asked her, afterwards, she said that it had risen like a worm in the shoulder, more swollen than anything, as if there were silver in the flesh as it burst from the bone; the pain departed from that bone and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while later it returned throughout the limb, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it often returned to its place, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered how he managed to move about without wanting this sickness in this way.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues. Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are various, according to their appearance and the nature of the wound or the pain they soak up.</start_of_turn>
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.
