And pulled out an arrow from the belly of a woman who was thought to be dying; and after she had been without feeling for XXX days, I cut above the arrow and bound it, and pulled it out without mishap
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a woman has an arrow lodged under the skin or in the back, and there is a deep wound above; and I pulled out the arrow from within, and did not bind its natural dispositions, and did not find any discomfort in any of her natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man had an arrow in his face, and there was a deep wound; and he suffered great pain; and there were many other things like that
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And she pulled out a splinter at home of the princes the king, that it was stuck deeply in the flesh of the heel and there was a great decline at the outer part; and the splinter was all restored. I was called to the cure after that when it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very inflamed.</start_of_turn>
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would keep it all very still and do not feel it; and there was no tingling or pain on the outer ear.</start_of_turn
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the point of the splinter. I put on the dressing an emollient plaster, so that it did not swell; and it appeared to me that the splinter had come out.</start_of_turn
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept it for the days, and healed the wound completely, and reassured the patient for a long time, until he said that the splinter was no longer in his heel; and he told me.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed upon the wound the corrosive medicine of vinegar by hand, until it was overdone, and I held it, and I felt the head of the splinter which was coming out at the root; then I closed the wound with that vinegar medicine, as long as the head of the splinter appeared visibly; and it healed well in three months, and then it grew so that I could remove the sutures, and I held one part and the other, and I could not bear it; so I ceased to suture and resorted to other methods of treatment, until I took it for the fourth time that the sutures were well made, as it is said at the end of this chapter, when I finished with it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it nonetheless, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me of the quality of the extraction of these arrows, if you place your cure upon that which I do not speak of, for the books do not teach me all; but you know masters better than I do much that is great, and that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, in descending order of the things that have been said in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not come out of the limb or are ficed by force, for there are two methods: either by pulling from the flesh or by cutting; and that which leaps forth by the heel or enters, it is an arrow that has pierced flesh, and leaps forth never more
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it until the flesh is swollen and painful; and even if it is pierced in the bone, and it cannot be drawn out, if you leave it for some days, and it moves every day; and then it leaps forth, and if it does not leap, if it is pierced throughout to the root, until the limb is swollen, and then you extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and there are no other symptoms that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not treat him for it, but leave it as it is, it will go away by itself after a few days, for if the splinter comes as far as the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is fixed only in the bone alone, and does not go as far as the surface, and remains in the patient for some days without any other accident, if the patient feels unwell, he must be treated for it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And remains the patient lying without moving for several days, if the fire of treatment should depart. If it has been moistened and cannot be stirred, if it is administered with tar, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the splinter is embedded in the bone so that it cannot be seen, if it has all its power; and if you feel it, if you treat it with no convenient instrument; and if you do not feel it, if there is no bone or nerve or vein, if the wound is large; then take out the splinter if you can, and if there is hearing in the splinter that it holds, if the bone that is split from two parts to the muscle that you take out, and then break or twist the ears of the splinter as much as you can, until you can take it out; and be careful not to break the splinter, that you take it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not manage it once, if the blood has clotted around the wound, then pull it out, for it is an alleviation.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if bleeding opposes the treatment, if necessary, remember what has been said in this chapter about the cure; and beware of incisions on the nerve and the vein, and put in place as you would move the arrow cautiously, neither too fast nor too slow, neither too tight nor too loose; and put the patient in the posture in which he was when the arrow went in, for that is the greatest aid of all, and if you cannot do that, follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees it or feels it secretly: then stretch it up as much as the pincers can take, and then remove it: if it spurts out now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	Therefore take hold of it immediately, as long as the nails can grasp it, and then extract it: if it leaps out now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be withdrawn, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it spurts out; and if the tip of the arrow is broken, if it has been broken, if you see it immediately, administer the curved instrument, so that the tip of the arrow is between the teeth of the instrument; and then extract it, and if the arrow is hooked, if it is hooked on the instrument, extract it with the point entering first, to ease the extraction.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the dressing is stuck, know that you must grasp all the hair around the wound or the venom is there. If you doubt it, then cure the wound as it should be cured.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the dressing is torn or stained with blood or pus, and it is close by, grasp it firmly; if you grasp it, keep hold of the wound and the nerves, then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tenailles used for extracting arrows is similar to the beak of an eel, and thus is this form.
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the outer end of the arm is like that of a bird’s wing, to push out the point of the dressing, as is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the teeth is such that they can bite and scratch if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the common teeth are blunt
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins that we must avoid in this place, which are 16 in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are covered by fat; and two arteries that are in the two temples that appear; and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are covered by hair; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two veins that are at the collar; and the two veins that are under the tongue.</start_of_turn
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly known are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the breast, and they call it the great vein; the second is called the median, and is composed of the cephalic and brachial, and they call it the arm vein; and the brachial is either on the left or right side of the breast, and they call it the belly vein, and is above the collarbone, and is the one from which we draw, which often appears above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the ulnar and ring finger, and if there are two veins; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is that which is below the curve of the left breast vein, and the second is the sole which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called the sural, which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins like these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of veins that are behind the ears helps to evacuate old blood clots and at emigration; and the quality of the blood, as I have told you, is that you raise the patient’s head and wipe the blood or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient’s neck with a screw, as long as the two veins behind the ears depend from the head: that is to say, if you see the pulse of your thumb, if it signs the clot; then take the lancet and pierce the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the entire vein above, and compress and the skin and the vein well two must pass through, and make the blood spurt out until you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries which are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, and soda, and oil, and at the root of the tears there are eyes; and the quality of the physician is like I have said: and the patient has strained his neck, so that the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse below his thumb, and then he signs the incision; then he takes hold of the thumb above his index finger, and pulls out the lancet below, and pulls the vein above, and the clot, as he has done in two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his need; then he releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on a bandage; and then the swelling subsides, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in relation to its swelling and extraction, or its beginning in the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is as valuable as that from the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the face of old age, and swelling, and redness; and the quality is such that if the patient turns his head to one side, as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument which is called the "scissors", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is as valuable as that from the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the face of old age, and swelling, and redness; and the quality is such that if the patient turns his head to one side, as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument which is called the "scissors", and place its point on the vein, and grip with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is whole and never again let any work be done with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not permitted that the flames be too strong; and the same with the air, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames break the bones when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are two cubits wide helps with the swelling, and the pain, and the redness, and the yellowness in the oil; and the quality of their blood is such that if the patient turns his head to either side, as before; then do the same, and let either the blood flow freely, or let it flow for a long distance with a broad flame, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is slight, by chance if it breaks; then make blood flow, as much as you are able, and then tie up tightly, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	When the blood of the vein does not suffice for drinking, and for food, and for diseases of the face, as with migraines and redness that come upon the face, and even when old; and when the quality of the blood is that the patient bites his throat, then grasp his hand with your left hand, take the burning flame that is long, and touch it to the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open very well indeed, and it is better to wait a little before beginning to correct; and do not go too quickly, but correct the blood according to your necessity, and leave it bound for one night, for it is very dry and restored. And this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps to loosen stiffness, and to cause swelling, and to cure diseases, and to stop haemorrhoids, and to dissolve corrodings, and to remove herpes, and to correct biliousness; and the quality of the blood is that the patient bites his throat from both sides, as we have said; and whether the master is standing over the patient’s head, and the patient sits on one seat, then grasp the vein long and wide, then take the blood slowly, or as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and gently pull the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to cause bloating in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and wounds of the lips, and toothaches and fevers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And when you are to make the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left side, and know them by their blackness, and because they have small black veins running through them: close both of them; but if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if you close the greater one from the lower part, and both of the smaller ones below and above, for this is a safe method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And of the blood of the lower lip the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins which are below the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and you touch the tongue, and look below each rib towards the costal margin of a black vein: close both of them, and do not move them too much, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that we commonly treat are usually sound; they can be cured in two ways: either by pricking them with a large flame or with an olive twig as with trenchant cuts, and this is called ‘anesil’; and they are large and subtle according to the size and shape of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the blunt needle is well known, and is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is another method for opening the large veins filled with visible blood, which contains blood and blood clots; and this is the form of the olive flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier the small veins, or there is small yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to alleviate diseases such as hiccups, colds, hoarseness, pain in the side, and pain in the belly; and it is useful to know that it is linked to the artery which is opposite to it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it grasps the bone, and blood flows, if it must be held back, as I have said; and it should not be grasped too tightly, but rather like an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the pulse does not clearly show its passage, if you must extract it, and bind another; or you wish no more of it, or you leave in its place the vein filled with blood in the arm: it will show clearly; and grasp the flame as little as possible, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the limb of blood flow, if you must therefore extract the limb, touch the limb until you know the pulse; then mark the place, and then bind the limb, and grasp the vein from the flame; and beware that you do not injure the artery when you see the limb swell, for it is the artery: stop immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see swelling high up like the urine of a child, and it is pale and limp, know that it is without an artery: haste then, and put your thumb on its length, and press your thumb until it stops bleeding; for this often happens. If the blood spurts out of the arm, leave it still and do not move the patient; and be calm, and do not move until it stops bleeding.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not stained, and it is painful, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts open, because the head of the retractor is withdrawn; staunch it immediately.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bandage of silk and lay it on, and take half of it and place it on well until the other half; if it stops bleeding, that is good; if not, if the physician wishes, as we have said, powders that stop bleeding; for the bleeding does not clot in many positions except for the small size of the wound, and the quality of the blood.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to heal blood vessels above, and bones below, because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic nerves, as we have said; and it is necessary for the patient to suffer through the nerve which is below, and if it is not sufficiently deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the blood clots either burst, or by chance cannot heal; and this nerve is often opened, and if it is not opened in some people because of its subtlety, it is necessary to take the blood from an anesthetic instrument; and withdraw the nerve from your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a bundle between the two nerves, if it is long enough.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic nerve helps to heal blood vessels above, and aids in the healing of the eyes; and it is necessary to cauterize with the olive or mirtle flame, because this is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is appropriate to inquire more gently at first, and do not grieve if it does not succeed the first time; and by chance it will swell up in some homes, which cannot be done the first time, but it does not grieve.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that blood should not be drawn except for the preservation of health and the avoidance of future diseases; and blood should be drawn from one of the three veins that are or should be: that is to say, cephalic, fast, or basilar. It must be drawn at the beginning of prayer before eating, and after eating when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be drawn for the first hour or the third, after two hours or three hours of the hour.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood that is drawn for diseases has no fixed time, but only when necessary for a wound or a nut, in all hours and at all times; and it is not permissible to draw blood from children until they are twelve years old, nor from women for more than four months up to seven months
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It is not permitted to give medicine to those who have passed sixty years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone feels well, in whatever way, if it comes to conceiving the intestines with a slight distension, if there be retained feces, so that the veins do not extract from the intestines the superfluous humors that are nourishing to the principal members; do not allow anyone who is too fat with meat, or who is drunk, or who is forced, neither hydropics; and if he suffers from well-being after eating, vomiting, and abdominal discomfort, and multiple bowel movements, and sleeplessness, and guarding, and fasting, and this whichsoever virtue, or by anything of the weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not great, by meats, and drinks, and medicines, if you have the power; then drink or bathe, so that nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood, and leave you with the vein full to the third, as we have said; and keep him engaged in work, and in drinking, and in luxury, and in similar things; and keep him bound and joyful, and let the patient be higher than he was before, and gently stroke his arm two or three times, then draw the thread from below middle, for when it is too taut or loose, it will not be able to correct itself; then stroke the limb with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the patient with a spoonful of oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein below the limb a spoonful or so, until he feels well, that the vein does not swell and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For some veins, when they are full like strings in a bow, if they have such an abundance of wind, that when one puts the flame on them, they recoil from the flame and do not open; and thus one is left with this; and if they are opened, the wound is too wide, for in this case it is necessary that the bowstring be warned of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; but if it bursts again, it must be stopped once and for all, or it will not be healed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the wound is infected, and the patient groans, leaving one or two days without joining the limb: by chance there will be pus; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; and if the wound is small, or if there is no apparent cause for such a flow of blood, as you see, if you believe that there is not much blood lost, although you see the flame directly over it; and do the work cautiously, even if the wound is infected; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, if you do not wish to renew the blood, put on a bandage of oil, for it softens the flesh of blood; and it makes the blood thicker in this limb. And administer the oil bandage on the wound so that you close the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this itself makes swelling and swelling of the eyes, when put on the limb; if it is too subtle it escapes when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, even if it is not dangerous except for this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are in a hurry, put on a soaked sponge and a bandage and strain for an hour; and it is recommended that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after some days no blackness or greenness, if it does not cause me harm; and if you see it, do not put anything else on it like aloe or mastic root in vinegar, mustard, or the like.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male. Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark red, leave it as long as it is dark; and if you see it thick, leave it as long as it is thin; and if it is too pale, leave it cool.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be known to the one who is plain and strong, and has the mastery of extraction of blood, that you should make the wound larger, and the flames larger; and to him who is weak, do the contrary, and make it healthier rather than worse, and must do so by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from the damage of blood and nerves, and is worth more than bleeding for a long time than for a short time.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him who has a cold constitution, it is to be given soft bread soaked in the juice of green apples; if he is faint, give him blood three times or four. And if he is of a cold complexion, mix before the blood soft bread soaked in beeswax, or in aromatic beeswax with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks at the blood, after the issue of blood, it is prudent that he emit a gruel of blood, and a fragrant slime, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.

For there is blood in the body which is already clotted, and causes fever; if it is prudent to extract a great quantity, and to dilate the opening as much as it screams in pain; then that you reward all the blood conditions, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not reappear in place of the pain, and this often happens when the patient is negligent; and do not do so except when you see the limb slipping, and make the blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, that you extend the limb immediately, because that would be bad; but leave it as it is when it is well the second time; or you point at the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein is forced out, and put on some oil and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain it, as long as the incision is calm.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein which is in the arm is blue instead of red because it is composed of blood.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	If the patient grasps his hand in hot water, while the flesh is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound opens well; and pull the limb through, neither too wide nor too long; or cut a large opening and draw the skin well up to the joint of the hand, and if it does not suffice, grasp the hand once more in hot water and leave the blood to clot in the wound, until you have enough; and if it is in this state, do not return the hand to the hot water, for more is put into it than in this; and the blood from this vein is more valuable than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the saliva of the right hand is valuable for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and immerse it in hot water, until the vein is emptied if we see it; and if it is pulled through, and if you press on it throughout, if it does not swell; and do not press too hard, for the nerves are all exposed without flesh, and then grasp the hand once more in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as well as you can, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will help to heal quickly, and make a soft dressing.</start_of_turn

Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies. When the patient has a cold fever, and his joints are swollen from the heat, and the veins are full of blood; and if the veins are in the ankle, or below the knee, from there comes drops of urine; the same as if there were a large wound there, or at the ankle, that the urine comes out in greater quantity.

And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you keep it warm from the cold that comes from outside, and the health of the passage is as if you were cutting; and be careful not to burn it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be put back, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient’s blood has to be let for the first time, if it starts again later, because the flesh is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the same with the other limb equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pulse of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its color is like the color of blood when it is hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient drinks or bathes, and the wound is strained at the ankle for two thumbs, for otherwise it will not open; and if it opens, do so in all ways you can, and through and through; and it is better that you close it, for the wound is already sore, and it is better to leave it alone with the hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find any bleeding from the wound that is opening or discharging pus, from the little toe downwards; keep the patient still and guard the area; do as much to staunch the bleeding as you see fit, and then remove the dressing, and apply a bandage.
