des sainies de ventouse	of air bubbles.</start_of_turn
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction which is done by cutting if it is with two methods: either it is very hot or very cold; and a suction that is made by cutting and extracting blood if it is done in twelve pulses of the wrist, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is in the collar; and two others in the two ribs of the collar; and the suction below the chin; and the suction of the two scapulae; and the suction on the buttocks; and the suctions in the two arms; and the suctions of the two legs; and the suctions of the two ankles; and the suction does not treat any wound, except for minor veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not cause any pain, as we do when we make a bloodletting; and it should only be administered, neither very hot nor very cold, in no disease that comes from repletion, until all the pulses are emptied.</start_of_turn
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to wind, or by custom, if the physician notes that the patient has coughed for some hour at the beginning or at the end of a month, or at any time, and if he makes a grimace or sighs in every tension; for there are some who, when they must wind, have a heavy head; and some who feel swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and at the collar, and dark circles under their eyes; and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth and have spit out the tongue and vomited blood. And some who dream of these things and see nothing but blood and death and fear and many other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when the patient has swallowed for two hours, we command them to vomit.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps for the pain of the head … that comes from these dark circles under the eyes; and it must not be used until all the fat has been evacuated; for this blowing out is useful in place of the cephalic blood, and must only be used for those who have a cold complexion or who are choleric, for this causes great discomfort; and for this reason it must be used with caution, only in those who have neither cold nor choleric diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who remains silent after that, if he becomes suspicious, must therefore put the suction tube one place further down due to the doubt of suspicion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind blowing in the neck is in lieu of blood from the head and from the brains, and for this reason it is worth to extend the pressure of the thumb, to open the channel of the beard, and in all things, and to cause swelling; and it is to be known that if it is held too tightly, it can cause strangulation or swelling of the stomach or the chest.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind that blows in the neck is worth as much as the pains of the head, and swelling and nausea, and strangulation, and toothache; and it is in lieu of the blood of the brains; and it is to be known that you must order the patient to move his hand to put it there, that he does not clamp the artery, and does not cause the evacuation of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windsings cause such diseases of the mouth as disease of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in lieu of the remedies of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are harmful to health, as they arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind that blows in the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and order the patient not to press too hard, because the flesh is sensitive, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is very painful, causing swelling of the underlying tissues and various diseases. It is therefore necessary that the dressing be large and of fine mesh, that it should adhere well; and by chance, if it should be too tight, it may burst, causing great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The dressings on the legs swell widely, for they draw blood from all over the body, causing old wounds of the groin, of the kidneys, and the bladder, and bring swelling of the flowers; and are in the place of the groin bones, and the calves, and all of them cause the body to swell after a long time, and bring vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the dressing is that you must first empty it thoroughly, and then apply it steadily, and hold it firmly in place, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the flesh red and swollen, and open up the blood; then rest, and put the dressing back on, and take care of the body, for there are some who have had their share of suffering, and who have open pores: if you must cut once only, and you must make large wounds, and a deep wound; and do so gently
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, it is sufficient to wound it three times: the first time to open the way for the large blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, it is sufficient to wound it three times: the first time to open the way for the large blood vessel. And when we want to drain blood somewhat and somewhat, we suffice with one wound only.</start_of_turn>
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed excessively, if we renew the process too often; if it is not expected, if there is great fear, and if the limb is perforated, it is finished; for he who has thick skin and hard bones, and who has many pores, must take the lead of the wound-healing oils, stimulating and dissolving: if it is for fat, violet oil or sweet almond oil or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is for blood, cresson oil or ivy or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if you take marigold oil, or balsam oil, or angelica oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If he has thick hair and large pores, it is not permissible to put oil on, but it is permissible to wash afterwards with rose water or cold water or pomegranate water or cucumber water or porcelain water or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or with rose water, or elderberry, and sumac, or similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And he who has excessive sweating should rise from wine strong, or from seawater, or from decoction of ivy or chamomile, or from other similar things; and he must not cover himself with a bandage before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and he must not sleep after the ventosation, and must rise when he is expected to rise and when he is risen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard him who is feverish from eating too much and inflamed; if he must take cold things, as grapes and cucumbers and lettuce easily, and similar things; and eat barley bread, and broth, and moist meats.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, if he takes honey syrup, and fragrant wine medium, which is between strong and new, and eat little, and eat barley bread and small fish and herbs; and when he sweats, he must drink more than he eats; and it is not permissible for anyone to give him any wine before or after the sweating, in order to comfort the principal members; and be discreet with it, but he must not abstain from it.</start_of_turn
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are inflicted on the belly, and on the heel, on the foot, and on the belly and the buttocks and the groin and the hip, for these members do not suffer from external wounds, and one does not force them except to draw blood from member to member; for to remove the viscosity which is in the member, as when we apply them to the nipples when they are full; and to alleviate the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, for by their attractive virtue they pull out the swelling or discharge the stone from its place; and thus they become erect when applied to the belly and the heel when there is retained wind; and these wounds are administered empty without any liquid, and never together with water that is cold or tepid, except in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the wound with warm water or water or herbs that are congruent with this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister administered with fire is like this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And he has two large and half palms of barley, or cost the entrance a little wound, as when a needle is pulled out, or be of hair, soft before if it does not harm the patient when putting it on the limb; and in the middle there is a stick of barley or iron, to put a bandage, and be of great and small size according to the diseases and the severity of those who take them; for the blisters of the sick are other than meats, and fats rather than oils.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must put this bandage on the limb: grasp the bandage with the loop or thread, and put it through the stick which is through the bandage, so that it tightens either at the back of the bandage that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and two must be either on the wound that we have said, or on the tip of the limb, so that when we pull, if it goes out, we take the bandage away; and grasp the thread as before, and do it often, if you have to manage.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the chest where it is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all times, there is neither swelling nor rupture, and it is only administered when it is clear of swelling, and is placed on the limb only slightly; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	There are no swellings or ruptures that necessitate the administration of the chest [pleuresin treatment] except in the limbs where it is not possible to place a chest [pleuresin treatment] due to its small size, such as with levres and gums, and similar things; and in those that are bare of hair, such as toes or nails, and others; and if the user finds that the chest [pleuresin treatment] that is in soft and clear water does not cause any pain, he should take it; and put a little warmth on it until it is warm to the touch, and remove the chest [pleuresin treatment]; and when it is full and soft, if it is possible to place the chest [pleuresin treatment] on, it should be placed there, for this is better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, if you lift the limb easily, and then with sharpness, move it well, and then release it; if the limb still swells too much afterwards, if you pour a cloth of flax on cold water, put on, until the swelling is diminished; and if the swelling is multiplied, put on pounded vitriol, or alum, or similar things, until the swelling is diminished; or you take out half of the fever blisters, and leave them until they dry on the limb, if it stops now; if you still have a great deal of swelling, take on other splints.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the swelling does not subside, if you wipe the limb with fresh blood, or you insert a needle into it until the swelling subsides, and then put on, as long as it feels the blood, until it is dried; and when you see that it is bleeding, if you sprinkle on some alum and ointment, or charcoal, if it will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear me, dear son, for in this chapter the learned men of our land marvel at this book, for they have never seen such things written in any ancient book, neither in letters nor in any other way; and for this reason this science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good authority on the subject. I know of nothing save what I have learned from the ancient books, or from my own studies and from experience, and from the customs of my life; and I have set out in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, just as I did in the two chapters which precede this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue to this book should be the sum of words and the chapters or the learned men put their understanding into them, and remain steadfast on the truth, so that those who are proved to know and learn this noble art, and learn from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if it is urgent to save the patient’s life on one side or the other, if nothing else can be done, if there is weakness of the limbs, or if the patient is a feeble or old person; or if the tension is not very strong or too cold; and mix cold baths, that is to say cold showers, and oil and laurel bath, and do not drink wine, do not eat fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is no further risk of fracture or swelling of the limb. If the patient recovers before the next morning, let him take the first opportunity to regain his former governance as he used to have.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones break start to restore, if you think that one must nourish the patient with foods that make great nourishment, or if there is viscosity, as with flour mixed in water, and peas, and testicles, and spleen, and spleenic pain, and fish, and great wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a part of nourishment, rest and more the fracture will mend.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Know that bones that are broken in parts or decrepit do not mend well by themselves according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs; neither are those that are too tender, as bones of small children. But there is no cure for them, so you must support the broken bone with great tension which has appeared and join the limb together, so that it is as strong as before; and do not let it move from its place, for this is what causes nourishment of large quantities of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And sometimes there is a sign that indicates its fracture, and its own instrument in restoration, as it is remembered; and it is known that the breaking of the bone is when it is twisted, and opens widely by pushing, and some by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have twisting, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is impossible for me to move the limb, but you bring medicines that come after, then restrain it now cautiously.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the wounds which break that go into the marrow, and are two parts of the joint, it is now necessary to put them right equally, even as abscesses which come afterwards; and if abscesses come afterwards, if you leave no mark, as long as the abscess is appeased; then put them right alongside the bone as you wish gently and safely, and the wounds which restored themselves are more gentle than those which remained there or had parts. Then strain, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they are two parts, if they are hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or a string and your hand; and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb break they are loosened, remember by all means the addition in their place at the bone that you wish, and keep that in your work does not cause any wound or pain to the patient; and adjust well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is good and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come by their work an abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a joint, if the patient is very sick and does not move it, whether awake or asleep, or turning or in any other way; and keep the limb securely so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, if it is not at a joint, and you must put it into use without feeling pain; and keep it straight, that it does not twist when it is restored; and the quality of the limb is as I have told you.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limbs are of various sizes in their breadth and length and shape.</start_of_turn
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as hands and feet and the like: if you can cover them with soft and subtle cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: if you can cover them with a broad and hard cloth, because the large cloth embraces the whole large limb and restricts it equally, so that there is no tension; then loosen the bandage gently, three turns or four according to the limb, and constrain the hand one inch at the whole limb, then go up to the break and constrain less, than the break then lets go one inch of the break; and soften the cloth somewhat and somewhat, as long as you take a large part of the limb still sound, then take back one inch of the cloth, and twist the bandage back straight over the limb break; then put back the part below the break, and constrain moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said at the first hour above; then put between the bandages soft cloth or cloth, until they are even all around, and then tie everything up with a knot, and then put your stitches well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is swelling or abscess, put upon something soothing the abscess outwardly, and which will soften the swelling, and leave it for a few days; then strain over your toes, and let them be half of a large cane resting firmly, or of splints made of wood, or of barley straw, and let them be in this fashion.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint that one puts upon the fracture be greater and broader than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the limb in breadth or length; then strain over the toes in the same way as before; and tie under a thread without fail, as before under the fracture; the more tightly it is bound, the less. And let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen; for if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their threads of linen cord, that is a great mistake, because the thread will not be equal if it is too subtle, and it will not hold properly.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is bruised by the nails after the stripping in the flesh, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with a broken bone, and the marrow is broken, I will speak of the cure later on
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And soaks that he cannot otherwise restrain must be stripped from these bones to break them at first hand.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it is not proper to put these stakes in place except after five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the afterburn; and when this is done, the method of ancient plasters is useful for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that is kept beside the mill, mix it with an abundance of eggs, and make this confection, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of plastering that restores fracture in many positions, and is equally useful for women and for small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains, linseed, alum, saffron, and Arabic gum, and mix them with vinegar; mix mirra and aloes, with vinegar; mix alechil with vinegar; and grind them up, and mix them with eggs; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this dressing, for it is made of good materials and will restore the fractured bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is useful for torsion: take mugwort and chamomile, each in quantity X; myrrh and aloes, each in quantity VIIII; acacia in quantity VI; mastic of Armenia in quantity X, and grind them well, and mix with water or eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones that have dislocated, relieve the pain that arises, and reduce the swelling of the bone, and the stiffness: take new linen, moisten it in oil and water, and put it on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These methods do not restore them immediately, but they are good for relieving post-traumatic swelling and pain, and restoring bones correctly.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another means of displacement that restores fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones involve restoring the fracture of the bone and diminishing the remaining swelling.</start_of_turn
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chamomile, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, barley flour, meadowsweet, one part of rue; grind them up, mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar or water, and apply.</start_of_turn
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of repositioning are more forceful than the first, when the abscess hardens during restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, and flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and fennel, and violets and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates does not put anything on the broken limb to restore its force except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen deems that one must put something warm upon the broken limb to restore it, such as wax and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poème oil, and gum arabic, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone of the limb moved; if not, loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen it, and stabilize the displacement immediately; and apply a light bandage, and a wet sponge of sea salt, and immerse in water, and lift up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is calmed; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry lint, moistened in water or oil of rose, and bind with a nut, until you are certain that the abscess has gone; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and make the pain cease, then recommence the gentle manipulation, and another displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around the bone, and that it is renewed, as you did the first time, you must provide support and lian, if necessary.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not occur in the limb anything that we have said, if it must be released, do not release it before three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, as we see, until the bruise has disappeared and the limb approaches its normal position; then restrain it more than before, and swell the limb, as I have said above; and if you see the limb dry out more than usual, do not delay, for as many times as you release it, cut a thread every time, and make a slip knot. By this means you will shorten the swelling in the limb and restore the limb to its proper position: that is bad, and if there is great fear, I see no other remedy but to leave it alone and treat it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are seen, and various figures, and the causes are manifold; for there are fractures caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collar bone fractured throughout to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as in the case of a fracture by splinters; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For when the spear pierces the bone from beneath in a forward direction, and is called this kind of fracture «absolue»; and the wound of these fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or displacement of the bone, or swelling on the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture of bone that approaches the skin, which is under the skin or on the skin, this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has penetrated the bone is as subtle as a nail, and the fracture is slight, and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "capillaire"; and if the wound is made or caused by a stone, or by a thorn, or by something similar, and causes the piece of the bone below to enter the cavity, and the limb is displaced as when the cauldron is carried when it is full; between the bone and the skin.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft bones or heads of children; and it happens in all these ways that small pieces are loosened from them like stars; and I will speak of it in detail later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus, we know of all these breaks by the tearing above them, the questioning of tensions, and the corrupt matter which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by that which when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe on it above, if the black break is opened
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s pain, and if you see no bad accident, as vomiting of bile, emission of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes grow pale and flushed, and other similar things in various positions, if not cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an imminent accident, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes first to you, and it is in the armpit, if so, it is right to remove the bone from its fourteenth part from the muscle that you must touch.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you are hasty to remove the bone from its seventh part from the bone that you must touch, then the tissue of the bone will be corrupted, and there will come the accident that we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a break of the bone comes up to the scalp that covers the brain, if you do that, you must cut off the split part: and that is that you take the head of the patient and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and on the figure of the wound more deeply than you can; and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or incisions, do what is useful, and that you fill the wound with moist cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the incisions have subsided, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then when the fracture has been set, it is done in two ways: one way if the nail of the fracture is narrow in front, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And so, if you have various sized nails, some thin and some thick, and they are pointed or iron-tipped, and in lighter work, that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and tough, if you must pierce through, even though you administer nails with washers, do not pierce through anything other than the outer surface of the bone; and must have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if the nails are withdrawn from the depth of the bone, if you have washers for all tests, this is the form of two nails.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through a brittle bone is that you put one washer on the bone, and turn your thumbs until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the washer back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisors of the space between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have reached the bone in your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pliers, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	When the bone is pierced and treated, if it is possible, reset the socket that has come loose from the bone to any other instrument resembling a chisel, but make it more tense and flexible than the other chisel; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not fear any scales, if the bones rest lightly on some instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more moist; and the load is very great, and that is his word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, whether it be a break or a fracture, so that when you have uncovered that part, you shall put in place again the head of this incisor lens, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut too deeply from one side, for the part that is hanging in two costs, if the cut is toward the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you gently press the bone all around, and take good care of the cloth that is soaked; for if it is outside the bone, if the bone rests lightly, because it is well placed in its place, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks through the skin does not pierce completely, and is only cut slightly from beneath, and there are small pieces, if you can restore the smoothness, and remove the splinters with a blunt scraper of various sizes, so as to bring about the most convenient healing, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is much scraping beforehand, and afterwards more subtly, and does not cease doing so until it is well done
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In the other sizes of capillary tubes and cuts, it is convenient to cause the lesion according to its location; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not studied this art
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the tip of the jaw is discovered, take a drape of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in olive oil, and put it on the wound; then take another drape doubled in two or three, and wet it in wine and olive oil, and put it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not damage the jaw, then administer by mouth another line of medicine, and do not restrain it more than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of iris, and oatmeal, and incense powder, and an apothecary, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer adequate medicines with the taste of medicine. Keep the wound clean, do not leave it bloody, do not leave it to gather pus, for when pus gathers on the wound it swells and causes great harm; for when anything biting is put on the jaw, if it is not done by mouth.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there be any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If black bile does not come forcefully except by the medicine that has been placed upon it, that some good has been done; so it is prudent that you take part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drapel, and put it upon the surface; then it will be cured in the manner of cures that it ought to be, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then the treatment consists of various cures that must be used as long as the patient is well.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if it is prudent that you swallow your small toe or nail, and put equal healing into your index finger and the pouch by driving it out, until it returns to its natural position; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros. Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must break the limb in another place if the break is there; and let the dressing be so thick that it fills the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should mingle the tents in the burrow, and die each for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis. And never should one put goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is too much snow drape over it, and hold the brim, and blow the patient among them; or do as you please.</start_of_turn>

de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no break of the bone, except for the teeth which are loosened, if you know it lightly.

It is advisable, if the fracture is in the lower part, to bite your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you have your right index finger of the right hand, and hold the fracture lightly, and hold the other side by force, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in.ij., if you must, that you administer extension of.ij. parts, as long as they are equal.

de la forcele	because of force.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful rupture has occurred several times previously in this area, near the shoulder, and if it is broken in two places, there are pieces, and it is more light to restore; or if there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is when there is a wound, you must have two assistants, so that one holds the limb that feels the forceful rupture; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the break back in its place so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend further, put under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of wax, or linen, as thick as you need; and extend and hold the forceful rupture, and strain the ball with your hand, so that you can put the break back in its place as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you are unable to support the arm's weight, because it hangs down, know that the patient lies supine on his belly, and put a cushion under the elbow, that is, the middle of the forearm, and hold the minister of the elbow forward, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris there, know that you must make an incision there; and remove the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be reunited by any support, if the head rests on one of the incisors that you have; but that you place a cushion under the arm itself, in order to protect the face.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, but is not curved, and be as wide as it seems convenient, according to the size of the bone and the possibility of the work; and there be two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the curve of the wound that you made when you treated the bone; and when you are assured of the suture, if the wound is small, or you doubt the suture, if employ the wound with patches and stitches, according to its quantity.

Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stiffness of the bone, when it is sensible to wounds and to the saw, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the fine powder of mill and of egg-white, and put on soft stockings, and put a ball of lead on the hip, if you are able; then take a great bandage of a palm of a hand, then put on a double drape on the stockings, and plaster; then take a slender splint of three fingers wide and long, and encircle that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains pendant; and put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the collar, and take off the hip bandage, and take off the painful hip; and leave the part resting, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture together, and you see clearly that the splint does not move from the broken bone, if you raise the limb cautiously, and if it is loosened, if you tie it; and manage the patient on his back, and put under his hip a little pillow, to raise the limb up; if you align the fracture by aligning the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it unless it is absolutely necessary until twenty days; then repeat the plastering, if you see that it is necessary, and strain and leave it in place, until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty days, and in less time to most men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the manipulation, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and support it firmly until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and less in most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is broken or widened, do not pull it out by force except by touch; if the limb appears according to the fracture pattern, and is reset according to its natural form, in all ways as you wish; then put on the limb powder with abundance of eggshell, and bandage lightly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle staple, a little wider than the scapula, and when the staple is fixed firmly in no part of the scapula, if you use the staple of hemp, so that the staple rests evenly; and then strain it with a great firm bend, so that the staple does not move from its place, and watch the skin of each joint; and every time it swells, if you strain, and put the staple back in its place if it has come loose from its place, and lie the patient down on his side; and the scapula is restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if the bone is fractured, and so be careful, for this is not a bone that easily breaks.

de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone thrust forward, and not a little like before, if it stays there, and the bone, do as we said at the fracture of the forceps to appease the afterburn.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is never broken in the middle, but this often happens; but it often breaks when it is pushed.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it declines downward, and causes the patient great pain, and there is no relief, vomiting blood, and loosening teeth in the fractured bone, and all this together.

And if a piece of the bone thrust forward, and not a little like before, if it stays there, and the bone, do as we said at the fracture of the forceps to appease the afterburn. And the restoration is that the patient lies again on his back, and puts in between the scapulae, then presses the scapulae, and reassembles the two ribs at the hands, and discreetly put all in equal manner that the figure of the bone is as it should; then put on bandages and bandage below the staple of salt, or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind above the fractured bone, so that it does not move; and turn the patient around the back, and restrain him gently, and reward somewhat every hour that the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, restrain it; and if you see that it is loosening, due to corrosion or by inflammation that comes to the limb, or pain or swelling, do not hesitate, and loosen it, and scrape away the dressing, and address what has come from the manner of treatment; then remend the dressing, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The ribs that break from the breast only come from the back, at the shoulder and do not bend except because they are slimy; and the pain is well known at the inquiry of two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is when you put the fracture back in its place as it should be
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then put on the dressing and bind it with a bandage if necessary
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is downward, if it causes great pain, and swelling, as if of pleura, for the bone is pressing on the gut; and there is vomiting, and all together there is great loss of blood, and that is a great grief, and many have died from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it must administer food that swells the belly, to push out the pain at its departure.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these chills have passed, life does not come again if it has not already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If it has already begun, then well.</start_of_turn
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one has ever put a bandage on the body to stop the fever, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the superfluous humours from the body by the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the wound with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on tents between the ribs to make equal the hour around, then either cure with the treatment for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the armpit, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is necessary to open the skin of the fractured bone, and if it is necessary to place a bandage, then one must cut through the bone, treat it gently, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with dressings until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus comes from the wound, put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and treat while the limb coincides with the wound, and do not leave the wound open or it must, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collar bone.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of a bone in the neck, or indeed at the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to no avail, and you see that it will be healed or not, if you take care if you see its hands softened and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel them
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wounds are mortal in many cases, and if you move them and feel well when you extract them and prick them, the union of the bone is saved, and the patient will be healed, if we put on treatment
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if anything similar comes to the shoulder blade, know whether it is whole or not; take care if the piece is softened, and if the accident is what is in the hands or on the back, there is an updraft of wind and discharge of the bowels; and when it is reminded on the belly, there is an updraft of discharge of the bowels.
