Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is reminded on the back and it is seen to be limp, it cannot be cured.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	The wounds are mortal: if you do not work diligently in their cure
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is less serious. If there is swelling, put on rose oil or yolk of egg on the spine; when it is calmed down, put on a comfortable and drying dressing, and bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest; do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If bones break, cover loosely over the wound; and unite the bones together, then support the joints of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, and bind it tightly; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "fracture of the heel", if it persists, turn your left thumb to the other hand at your wrist, and put them even, then put on the dressing and bandage, if necessary; then strain it, and if there are broken bones, if you keep it still, and unite them, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if there is no immediate sign of improvement at the head; and if it lasts long, and declines in the thighs, and brings pain to the patient at the place where it is fractured, and swelling ensues.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the restoration is to be made, extend your hand above the fracture, until you reach the fracture; and keep the fracture in place; and if the fracture is only at the head, put it in its natural position, until it is restored to its natural shape.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or declines downwards, make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set the hair even, if you put on a bandage, then put on a staple of wool or hair, and hold the bandage still, so that it does not move; and keep the limb relaxed, as long as the hair is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess bursts, do not touch it, until the abscess has subsided; then put on what we have mentioned before; and then return to rest, and hold it still if it is appropriate, without causing any further harm; this is the proper method.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And there are two methods for restoring it: one is to take a fistful of moist earth and shape it like this:
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should order the attendants to hold the limb firmly at its collar and to grasp the limb above the elbow with the fist of the hand that is not supporting it, and to hold down the forearm with the other hand, and to extend the forearm to its greatest extent.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, strain your hands against the breeze, and on the breeze, and extend your thumbs towards your side
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breeze is close to the shoulder, you must put your middle finger below the armpit and the other towards the heel, below the breeze; and if the breeze is towards the heel, you must put your little finger lightly, with force, until the breeze is even on the arm and the heel; then put the breeze back in its place, as it should be, and strain it, even if the armpit does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the wound does not come out, do not strain for more than thirteen days; put on a soft bandage and oil of rose, until the wound is calmed; then strain, and put the support on the bone, then assemble the limb on the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put on the bandage, strain on the aid, and on the limb, so that the limb is in its place, without anything hindering it, or without displacing the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not displaced, if you use pins, put on the bone a pin wider and stronger than the others, and leave between the pins a space equal to twice the thickness of the bone; then strain on the pins, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the shoulder blade slipping out of place, and the limb twisted, as we have said, when you restore the limb promptly, and doubt the incision, if you leave it closed until the seventh day, as we have said; then look carefully for three days afterward, that the swelling does not increase or that no redness spreads to the limb, or that the swelling does not recur in the limb because of excessive tension.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the arm hangs down, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such thing happens, if more than three days have passed, and the patient sleeps on his back and has his hands on his stomach; put a support under the limb one inch thick of wool equally, and look for an hour or two to see whether the limb is straightened or the ligaments are softened; if the dislocation is cured by the power of medicine, and you do as we have said before, in part as a remedy for the pain; and when it starts to recover, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and limb must be restored in forty days at the most; and then one must loosen them and administer poultices and medicines of ointments for the limb to recover.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is painful and bloody, if it remains for more than a day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	... for a fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and is close to the pouch, and the other is large and is close to the little finger; by chance the large bone only breaks sometimes, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, restoration is easy, and healing; but when the large bone is fractured, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when it is fractured whole.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if it is recommended to extend the limb slightly, and put it equal.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if the large bone is fractured, if it is recommended to grasp it more strongly; and extend over one cushion, and hold the wrist of the hand higher than the other, and the small hand lower than the other hand, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, and one cushion in front of him higher than the patient; then extend the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or to the shoulder, and another assistant at the other side.</start_of_turn
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he sets the eye equal, according to its better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If in the fracture it is broken into pieces, if you put something into its place, and if there is none that pricks it now, and you do not manage to restore it to its place, if you leave it and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If in the fracture it is broken into pieces, as I have mentioned in the singular concerning this chapter; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration blood spurts out, if it is thick I cover it with a coating of rose oil and white wax, neither too thick nor too thin; and I cover it from above secretly, until the spurting blood has ceased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then I apply the cerote, and I place a stuffing of fine powder with eggshells, because I put in the pins, and let the pin of the bone be more firm and wider than the others; and I make the wound have six pins or more in various positions: either that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and I stretch it more on the fracture than elsewhere, and I keep it together less often, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the draping that is on the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is used to tie it, be neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the limb and the joint afterwards each day.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any other evil accident comes to the limb, as if there is swelling in the limb, you must command that the limb be elevated with warm water, until the swelling is appeased; and leave the limb still resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the traction, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, if necessary
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not depart from the limb, because it is too great, then shalt thou soften it, namely by fomentation, and let it remain for some days, until the swelling depart, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not keep it bound for more than twenty days
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when the swelling has gone down, then let the patient hold his hands to his collar, and keep his collar even, and protect him from movement and contamination, and sleep on his back; and give him nourishment every thirty days or every fifty, or sometimes every twenty days, according to the composition and temperament of the virtues
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The bones at the back of the hand and two together cause many fractures, and only rain comes more often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is broken or rained on, if it is to be known that the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of him equally; then put his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the physician the broken bones, and put them equal with the eyes; and put on the plaster and the bandage, if there is no opening; then put on a splint as much as is necessary; and be covered with a cloth of linen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the shoulder blade under the belly of the limb, if you make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to hold his broken limb against his side; then strain from a long cloth, and be the splint as great as the limb, and strain it, as it is commanded.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is downwards, if you command me to place a splint above and another below, so that the hand is overspread and straight, then I will bind it tightly around the hand, and hold it between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break does not come from either side, if it is in the palm, if you command me to make it even, as it should be; and I will restrain it with the splint, and if you see that I must place a right-angle splint to raise the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, as in the index or one of the others, if you make it even, and I will bind it with the two fingers which follow; or you will bind them all together, holding them close together, as much as he wants, or you will place a splint above, as with a pouch; and take care of the restoration and the arrangement of the wound, and cure whatever comes of it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	And if the break does not come from either side, if it is in the palm, if you command me to make it even, as it should be; and I will restrain it with the splint, and if you see that I must place a right-angle splint to raise the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, as in the index or one of the others, if you make it even, and I will bind it with the two fingers which follow; or you will bind them all together, holding them close together, as much as he wants, or you will place a splint above, as with a pouch; and take care of the restoration and the arrangement of the wound, and cure whatever comes of it, as I have said.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the hip are often fractured, and one can see it when it turns frontward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound together again.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs symmetrically; and it is when the fracture is at the root of the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if a fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if one of the ligaments above the ankle is broken, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, and then either the ligament above the knee is fractured, or the lower ligament; then put the thumbs of both hands on the bone, so that it is in its natural position, and then put on the dressing and bind it, because if you do not, it will not heal.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a wound close to the eye, if you leave it calm for a while and then return to your work and your cure, the binding is made in part for safety.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a strong bandage doubled over twice or three times, and to remove the excess, then bend the limb until the talons reach the root of the nail, and pass a thread long between the thigh and the limb below the knee, from below the knee up to the top; then bend the limb and the thigh together, and put on the outer dressing and a stay.  Then put two threads of the same kind between the thigh and the limb as you passed before, and three stays that are below, and put back the thread at the top until you see below the piece; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any further damage.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is pain, if it comes loose, and address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to cauterize, as we have said; and if we cannot, it is necessary to cut the bone, and drain; and cure as we have said, when it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case when it is set in place, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in the restoration made in this way, I do not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And if the bone is set in place in one or two days, or less or more, according to the variety of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rue of Genoa</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hairs that in the groin district have recently burst, but they often break again.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If they break, if not only a tear, or an opening, and there is pain, swelling, and this feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure de la jambe	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hairs that on the leg have two bones, of which one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "fleshy part"; and they often break as it happens with the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all done in this way. And if both bones are fractured together, the leg is twisted in every part
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the bone is fractured in two, twist the limb forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the great bone is fractured, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it is twisted from its place.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When it has been found that the fracture is useful, restore it to its normal position and bind the limb evenly; however, if it breaks again, there are more pieces to be extracted, even if the extension is less severe and lighter; and do as your virtue dictates.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have completed your work, if you take two strips of coarse cloth that reach from under the armpit to under the knee of the limb, and bind the limb from one end to the other; then cover with two layers of bandage from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not be able to move forward or backward; and that is good; and no one should administer anything that will lengthen the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is a fracture, and there are many pieces, that the extension should be less violent and lighter; and adjust accordingly.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones it is known.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	As for the ankle, there is no fracture in it; but in the bones of the foot there is never a fracture and two are enough, and there is no other cause of death except for great swelling of the limb.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones pressing against one another, if you put the limb so that it appears to be floating in the air, as if a bird were flying by, and then put the limb back in its place, the bones will rise up; then put the bandage in place and bind the limb firmly, and put a little bandage under the foot at the joint, and strain the limb gently, and when the swelling has gone down cover the limb with cloth and other things as you think is necessary.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is still swollen, because you will find the bones whole, whether fractured or not.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said must be done with the hand; then put at the break a support according to the length of the break, and make it somewhat wider; and put on the thumb that which I have mentioned, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more breaks, break them, and put on over each break a support according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone. Make sure that the thumb remains above the break of the bone as much as possible, if it remains well-held.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have said about other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the limb is fractured and the limb is swollen, incline the limb towards the painful side and support it behind; then fill the limb with wool, putting as much in as a sto; then draw out the limb, leaving the back and front exposed, and then draw up the sto, until it reaches the entrance of the limb, and bring back the bone with the sto; and when she sees blood, if she has drawn the sto, and when she has bled, she will recover in seven days or eight: if the fracture is restored, and if you see that, take a bladder of urine and tie a string to the belly and pass the whole bladder into the limb; then blow in the string until the bladder is expelled: the limb will then restore the fracture; then fill it with wool and leave it for a few days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or a woman is fractured, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; these fractures are not hidden from the one who studies and uses them, and they are recorded in my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration: whether it be in this case or not
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put it on the arm; then wrap around it with cloths, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be completely healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as for the bones of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be set immediately, as the things we have said prove.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, if the restoration of vitriol suffice, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour, or the next, if there is no coming of the after-effects.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there comes swelling, if you must leave the restoration until next day, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch neither the third nor the fourth part, for you will bring about other evils.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is fractured is appears above like a wound discovered, then you must know that you must touch it lightly with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to set your hands equal, if the limb has this instrument which is of iron, which is two or three inches long, and its breadth is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it is necessary at the middle that it grasps three or four lines, according to what is necessary in the bruise; and be round and somewhat large, so that it does not swell to the compression on the limb at your work, and be above and forward, and large from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because it is considered that the curved limb should be placed over the head of the visible bone; and once it is put in place, as soon as it comes back, it should be equal on both sides
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, if you must cover the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone as we have said, if you see that the handle of an instrument that can be covered over is to be used, or to pierce or suture, to your poorness; then take away that which is remaining in the bone, rough and scaly.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, the limb is not naturally in its normal position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then immediately apply a black astringent poultice; and keep it in place; do not put any cerote or other thing on the wound, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars [medication] when the bone has been reset, and leave the wound uncovered, and keep the dressing tight around the wound, according to the extent of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has been done foolishly, and it has caused the patient to die or become lame or caused decay on many occasions; or the inflammation is milder and less painful than the other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the misfortune has passed, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to place it on supports; then cover around with cloth, instead of supports, a firm bandage, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see afterwards one or two days that the swelling has receded from the wound, if you put on anything on the whole time, and there is healing of wounds, as with tetracycline and similar medicines.</start_of_turn>
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you stretch the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, while it is soldered and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be gently flexed and straightened part by part like a bow that corrects itself lightly.</start_of_turn>
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists in displacement, and cannot be soldered but returns almost to its place, with small pieces of bone, for it is necessary that you reduce the wound with all your might, and that you extract all these broken pieces which cause this pain.</start_of_turn
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or any other kind of corruption, if you can cure it, according to what is said in this chapter above.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and is open on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the great limbs, if you do not treat it, for many times death comes from this; but leave it as long as it bleeds; by chance it will mend by itself after twenty days or thirty, and then cure the wound if you wish; if you do not wish, leave it.</start_of_turn>
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The hairs which come out of the beard.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The hairs which come out of the beard often follow the breaking of the wind, even when it is close to the joint; and it is a helpful thing to see the figure of the limb; for by chance one cannot make the limb do its natural work.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that we are aware: if he gives astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollus, acaice, and others, that you take neither of these things, or all together, and mix them with stiff wine or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and bind it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is set; and then reset it, and begin again, until the nodation is bony; or you bind it on a piece of well-made leather; for the property of leather is that it hardens all the swellings under the limb; and if the nodation has already hardened as much as a stone, and it is necessary to harden it, if the swelling above has burst, and make the excess apparent; or you must leave it alone, until it is bony, and treat it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that is weak after the treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is restored and remains weak afterwards, if there is any discomfort: because sometimes it is caused by the limb having been too tightly bound and not properly relaxed; or because there are too many bands, and they prevent the limb from moving smoothly; or because of many bruises; or because of too great a movement, not even in its place; or because there is blood in the tissue, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to feed the patient and make the limb firm, until the pain is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him merry and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts the great restoration, and the blood often boils fiercely, until the limb returns to its natural position; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is bent after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it retains its natural work: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have acted thus in our land; this work is blamed, and many evils result from it, and by chance the patient; although if the swellings and torture are fresh, if one covers them with hot water, or softens them with herbs such as rue, meadowsweet, and melilot, and similar things; and makes an emollient plaster, like aquaint well made, and takes the muscle of rue, and confirms it with gelatine grease or oil of poppy seed, and makes plaster over; or one takes fat figs, and pounds them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone fractured by continuous rubbing and length of time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Or do not cause movement to the limb immediately after its fracture
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, if it is covered with skin up to the bone, make a slight incision; and apply cushion and dressing to the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes about, if it can now be corrected in its original position
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if it swells up, and by chance when it is reset, it causes pain to the limb; therefore it must not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings about swelling and other pains; however, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have commanded the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint from the head to the wrist.</start_of_turn>
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The teeth are loosened and the jaw is dislocated in two ways: either the jawbone is fractured from its socket and softened, or it is loosened completely and hangs downwards, causing the tongue to hang out of the mouth, unable to be held in place, unable to close the mouth, and to be enveloped by speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns by itself in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If it is entire and complete, you must certainly hold the limb firmly and without fear; and in such a way that the servant grasps the chief of the patient, and holds the thumb of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand must be placed flat, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them in all parts
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep the eye fixed even, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arise with hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are restored equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed with gentle pressure, place upon moist cloths a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind firmly with linen bands; and let the patient rest on his back, and keep his arms still between two cushions, so that he does not move forward or backward, neither to the right nor the left, nor does he strain to speak; but take gentle nourishment, until the pain is gone, and keep the jaws still.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not manage to be reset at a single hour, and are not made firm at their roots, if in comes fever and swelling accustomed, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	from the forceps.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot pull out a wound that is deeply seated, and is always damaged when it is driven out, and it is always felt.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And if the patient lies perfectly still on his back, and extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then place the bandage and bind it, and hold it in place; the limb which is towards the heel cannot be dislocated; if it does so once, if you leave it in its place, as we have said; then place the bandage and bind it, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the shoulder will be restored when it is freed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation de l’espaule.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hairs that are too long at the shoulder are not loosened by anything except in three ways: Firstly, that they are loosened at the armpit downwards; and secondly, at the part of the wrist; and by chance at the part above, and this is enough; do not loosen them from behind the shoulder, or from the front, or more than once; and if several times they are loosened downwards towards the armpit, even among those who have little hair, for at these jumps they become immediately ill; and among those who have enough hair, the jumps become painful, and return to pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there occurs in some households a percussion or cracking, and it engulfs the swelling of an abscess with a thick discharge, and care must be taken that it is not damaged by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you suspend it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation is when it is pulled towards the armpit, and it makes a difference between the healthy shoulder and the sick shoulder; and you will find between their difference a bulge; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and the armpit touches the head of the shoulder, just as if there were a wound; and the patient cannot move their hand back to its place, neither make any movement; and in the same way, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you find it immediately on touching; and this method of dislocation is not enough to restore it, when it is new, or when the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician grasps the painful limb upwards, then puts the thumbs downwards on the buttocks, and grasps the joint firmly upwards to the bone; and the physician grasps the limb and extends it upwards, since it is put downwards.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said above, if you must, instruct the patient to bathe in warm water; and give him mollifying and soothing medicine, such as decoction of alum and fenugreek and melilot in water, or give it to him; then lie the patient on his back, and put under his buttocks a cushion of linen equal in size, neither too soft nor too hard, and put the thumb of the hand over the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant will hold the shoulder joint, so that it does not move backwards; the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains according to this method: that you make present one person who is greater than the patient; and two attendants will support the shoulder from the front, and support the shoulder from the buttocks of the patient, and keep the buttock up, so that the patient hangs down; and another attendant will treat the hand of the patient backwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is often repeated thus: if one grasps a stone of the length of a thumb and of the thickness of two fingers, and places it under the base of the thumb, and grasps the thumb with the other hand, and gently stretches it out, the joint will return to its place immediately; if it does not return by these means, do this cure: take two thumbs and three fingers of the width of a fist, and place their heads together at the crease of the palm, following this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place the thumb of the fist over the base of the arm, so that it does not move the patient; put it into the armpit; extend your arms above the arm of the patient; and hold the shoulder joint above the arm, and the arm at the wrist; put one elbow on one inch of the palm of the hand, and stretch out the hands backwards, or leave the forearm hanging down: the dislocation will now be regained.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is regained, in whatever way, if you put a ball of wool of equal size under the armpit, then put the plaster on the abscess with powdered oatmeal, with incense and egg-white, on the whole shoulder and around, and strain the armpit outwards again, and bind the limb over the plaster, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is commanded that he should move his arm until it is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move it more after five or six days, and it will be healed.  If it is stiff and is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been forced out by moisture or some other cause, you must administer three cauteries, as if it were placed before or behind the abscess.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it does not heal after twenty-five days, and the limb cannot be lifted, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are crushed or stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be fixed in its place again
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The shoulder dislocation that is at the side of the arm, and the arms, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and has received another support; and it heals as long as it is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And when the healing has passed, if there is stiffness in the limb and late mobility, if the patient uses the limb many times, as long as the stiffness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	because of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint of the shoulder has been damaged at several points, and has returned to its normal position; but it has been damaged throughout, both frontally and laterally, and the dislocation has not been corrected, as it is well seen and felt; and it is damaged in a certain way.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the oil, if he can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and cannot hold the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must keep it still in this way even after you have pulled it out, for if you pull it out again, if it comes out once more, it will be more painful to bring it back. And by chance it will not be able to be brought back at all, even if it is behind; for it is better to leave it as it is than to cause further dislocation, which is more painful and can lead to death.</start_of_turn>
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it can be restored, when it is like this that you can bring it back, you must extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down toward your belly according to the patient’s situation, front and back, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, if it returns when the hand doubles over its hand, and the thumb is firm at the root that is deshydrated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If he does not see it return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from its shoulder; and when you have wrapped around a double long and wide bandage; and when you look at the joint with the hand, if there is no oil on the joint to soften it, then join the joint firmly; and when it is in place, put on dry patches with eggshell, and the swelling will disappear, and bend the arm to the patient’s chest, and leave it for a while; then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	When the joint is firmly in place, if you release the limb and leave it, and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plaster and the limb, and leave it until it is firmly set; then you can release it.</start_of_turn>
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, bathe and rub well, and press until it is eased; or place upon the joint a fatty mutton nail, then leave it in for a night, and the bone, and wash; and when it sweats, gently wipe the joint, then put the nail back, and then wash again; do this twice or thrice until it is healed. If you see that it returns to its place, put upon it moist butter warmed with burr, and strain it; if it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the limb is loosened, and its return is laborious, more than any other joint throughout the body; you must therefore bring it back to its place immediately, even if it is loosened, and even if there is bleeding or infection.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put your hand on a table with the patient, extend the limb, and look at the hand, make it put its palm on the appearance of the joint, and press until it returns naturally, it is necessary that you watch if it is well in place; then put the hand back on the table at extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I will look and put his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that is well; if not, if the strain of the tendons is calmed by the after-treatment, and you leave it in its original position, let it resume its course.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you do not put it back after a while, it will remain dislocated; and it does no harm to the patient to leave it loose, and he cannot strain anything further: so that if the nerves are severed, or the artery; if there is no other cause for straining except to cauterize, do so in this case, and by chance that is the only thing that is worth doing.</start_of_turn
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the limb is in its place, if you place the displacement that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove and leave it in peace.</start_of_turn
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it easily, and there is no pain, if the fluid of hot water is applied, and it is rubbed until it is well healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the thumb detached from the wrist at the wrist-bone or at the palm or belly; therefore must the thumb stay fixed, and hold the dislocation back in their pouches until it returns, then support the head of the thumb, and guide it to the part where it is joined; and leave it for two days, and then put it back in its place; and do not touch it, as we have said, and withdraw from it, and make it move, and bind it; do this often, until it is straitened, and do the same if it is detached at the belly of the thumb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is detached from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	and do the same if it is loosened from the shoulder.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in danger.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign that it is that the blood egestions flow contrary to their usual course, it must not be held, and many times it softens no limb, or the two knees or two arms or the head; and many times the spleen moves to three parts. The one that moves at the back is called "gilbosite": the cure is that if the gilbosite comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, they say that the old methods of treatment were with great words, which did not yield much; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
