Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the heel, there is no healing; and that which comes directly on both sides, we cannot cure it except for that which comes from behind; as I have said; and that the patient’s face should be stretched out one inch wide, and should be strained from his knees up; then I take a fist and put it under the heel, and I put another hand over the toes, and I tie a thread around the patient’s ankle, and I take another hand and I take hold of the shin, and I tie two threads between the two toes; and let them be well closed, as I have said, and the patient should keep his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If she does not return by this remedy, take a cube of three hands' breadth long, and bind the part below the navel; let the patient lie on the side, and insert the head of the cube below the navel, and put the middle of the cube on the spine; and put the thumbs of both hands on the other head of the cube, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it at the wrist that twists at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If two veins are torn at the arm of the patient of a great size, and two others are torn, and between each twist of the vein there is a swelling and bruising, a palm of space long; and there is in each twist one puncture, or the wrist twists, and the twists must be firmly fixed, so that they do not move; and between each two twists there must be one twist returning, so that the loop which returns must be large enough for the wrist to pass through; and then join the loop which is between the elbows to the wrist of the patient, and the other loop to the pieces at the other wrist, and press the minister’s wrist at all the loop, and the master must put the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are even, if you put on a dry dressing with a great amount of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three fingers’ length, that will cause the swelling to recede and the sensitive part of the vertebra to become numb, then bind with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient take nourishment secretly until they are well; and if nothing else comes to an end of the well-being, if it is necessary, administer soothing and relaxing medicines, with the support that we have said before; and never give a dose of mercury, and never does it appear behind the scapula of the back, take care that it is not a dislocation; and the bone that is opened must not be presumed to be anything other than an accident: for in this case comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder only dislocate; it does not happen with other joints; and the hip joint is damaged in three parts: front and back, and top and bottom; the more it is damaged from the front, the more it is damaged from the back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And knowledge of its dislocation is such that when one joins the painful limb with the bandage, if it is longer and the patient’s knees are wider than the normal, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and it is the pus that is left from the abscess that comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this is that if this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this is that if it is well placed, the limb is well placed in accordance with the completion; however, do not double the knee excessively in pain, and if you see that it is suffering, do not delay, and retain the urine, and swell the limb, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that one who has it behind, if he cannot expand his knee, neither double it, and is that leg shorter than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is displaced from its socket.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If this semblance of dislocation persists, if it is an old dislocation, and it remains as it is without any cure; and one must not presume otherwise.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you rush to return the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance, if it returns, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary to apply a strong minister, and keep the limb firm with two hands, or one, as you please; and another minister stretches out his hand above in part as much as he can stretch out his hands below his buttocks, then he grasps it with a loop of thread above the knee; and another holds the head of the limb; and they stretch up and down together until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains so
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is very common in three out of four cases; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, if it is possible to cure its semblance, when the dislocation is in the armpit, it is possible to place the limb over the bony prominence of the shoulder, then put the limb over the root of the arm, and the limb which is beside the angulus, then stretch the limb upwards towards the armpit and towards the forcele; then take hold of the other limb of the patient and embrace the large prominence of the painful shoulder, and extend it towards the front: if it returns to its place now; this method of dislocation is the least severe of the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment. de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	When there is wound and dislocation together,
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not mindful of me and do not know how to cure it, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be bold; and begin with gentle treatments to the wound, and leave the patient in the hands of the Lord, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you restore the limb to its place, even if the wound has burst; and when the limb is restored, if you administer gentle treatments to the wound, and cure the wound, as it should be, from dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, if the bones are fractured, do as we have said in simple illnesses; and you must abstain from pride, as I have said, for this is harmful to you according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and body.
